Although District records are unclear as to the date, there were indications that the Plainview Sunrise Rotary Club surrendered its charter to Rotary International and ceased to exist during this Rotary year.

Governor Cook selected the following Rotarians to provide leadership in District Committees: Lon Moser - Secretary; Gene Shelburne - Treasurer; Olen and Edna Wilson - District Conference; John Dawson - Public Relations; John Heetland - District Relations; PDG Bill Hubbs (Pecos) Nominations; PDG J. D. Cage (Muleshoe) - Extension; Ron Bailey (Lubbock) - Free Enterprise; Jon Oden (Amarillo) - Resolutions; PDG Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) - PolioPlus; W. L. Goble (Levelland) - District Liability Insurance; Tommy Patterson (Southwest Lubbock) - Diabetic Camp and Community Service; Walter Johnson (Amarillo) - Boys’ RYLA; Larry Johnson (Odessa) - Girls’ RYLA; PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) - Rotary Foundation; Eldon Davidson (Amarillo East) - Group Study Exchange; PDG Bob Lewis (Big Spring) - Development, Planned, and Annual Giving; PDG Edward Self (Plainview) - Paul Harris Fellows; PDG Burnett Roberts (Levelland) - Special Matching Grants; Don Patterson (Amarillo West) - Charitable Trusts; John E. Goodman (Amarillo West) - Arch Klumph Award; Gary Moore (Amarillo West) - Club Service; Robert Holland III (Perryton) - Membership Development; Wayne Smith (Lamesa) Club Bulletins; Charles Taylor (Odessa) - Rotary Information; Boyd Williams (Shamrock) - Attendance; PDG Jack Selby (Lubbock) - Vocational Service; Scott Foster (Denver City) - Interact and Rotaract; PDG Louis Rochester (Odessa) - International Service; Ted Holder (Levelland) - World Community Service; and Lee George (Big Spring) - Youth Exchange.

(Editor’s note: Governor Cook was kind enough to submit a summary of his year. It is far more interesting than anything a search of his files produced so it is printed here.)

DISTIRCT 5730
1991 - 1992
BY PDG JAMES E. COOK

“I don’t recall ever hearing more inspiring addresses by Rotary International leadership than we heard at our 1991 International Assembly in Anaheim. These talks became the basis for the Governor’s club address, as well as seeing the direction R. I. leadership, coupled with the publishing of The Rotary Book of Wisdom by outgoing President Paulo Costa. This is a one page response by Rotarians in leadership as a reply to “Why I’m a Rotarian.” It was invaluable for examples in leadership.”

“My year encompassed the 75th anniversary of the Rotary Foundation. In recognition of Arch C. Klumph who started it with $26.50 left over from the Atlanta convention, we began the Arch Klumph Donor fund in District 5730. Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock) polished gem stones, which we gave to “Arch Klumph Fellows” as recognition for an individual’s gift of $26.50 to the fund.”

“President Saboo of India was an exceptionally good president. We had met President Saboo and his wife, Usha, at Zone Conference in Shreveport the previous October. He proved to be an easy, comfortable and courageous leader. He had survived an ad hoc challenge to the R.I. presidency by some of his own countrymen, but seemed to be accepted and respected by all who came to know him. The District also had the pleasure of his presence in Big Spring on May 28, 1992 to honor RI Director Ralph and Billye McLaughlin. We had the opportunity to spend the afternoon with him while our District Chairs presented our special programs and projects. Their presentations were excellent and President Saboo added his critiques, remarks and comments after each one. PDG Bob Lewis (Big Spring) was the moderator for this event. Some three to four hundred people attended the evening dinner at Howard County College. Highlights included the presence of all of the sitting District Governors from Texas, and Zone Governors from as far away as Nebraska. President Saboo and Director McLaughlin dedicated an oak tree on the campus of Howard Country College and we quickly dubbed the oak as the world’s first “Saboo Oak.” At the evening dinner Dr. Reddy (Big Spring) and Dr. Naidu (Odessa) presented a check for $10,000 to the District to establish a village Medical Clinic in India with a trust, and on receiving the check President Saboo asked, “Governor Jim, will you accept this for the District and see about finding a Special Matching Grant for this project?” Dr. Naidu told a story of being taught to write in the sand by his mother before she placed him for adoption in the United States. Her aim was to insure his education and she was successful for he became a cardiologist and a respected citizen of Odessa. President Saboo’s theme “Look Beyond Yourself” seemed very poignant that evening.”

“As I entered the Rotary year I knew that I must find out what others were doing successfully, capitalize on their areas of expertise, and help them network with others so that the District would be both cohesive and informed. That was a tall order for at the conclusion of our year of service we were amazed at the number of quality leaders we encountered in our clubs and district and the amount of Rotary that was taking place in all clubs, large and small. Rotarians were doing a marvelous job of living and being Rotary.”

“World Community Service was in the hands of PDG Louis Rochester (Odessa) who was ably assisted by Ted Holder (Levelland,) Dr. Michael Graves (Plainview,) and Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock.) Kyle Russell (Midland,) Julian Dawson (Kermit,) and clubs in Andrews, Pecos, Monahans, and Denver City had working relationships with clubs and groups in Mexico. We recognized their efforts and encouraged other clubs to join them in their endeavors in Mexico.”

“At PDG Charles Beil’s (Big Spring) Foundation Seminar held in Plainview in 1990 I addressed the subjects of the 3-H and Matching Grants programs. Then “an evangelical passing of the hat” collected $100. A drawing for the $100 donated was held to determine who would be the first Special Matching Grants Donor. Sammy Bigger’s (Southwest Lubbock) name was drawn. Others contributed including R.I. Director Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring.) During the rest of Governor Hubbs year and all of my year, that fund reached $2800.”

“District 5730 was matched with District 3710 in Korea for a Group Study Exchange in 1991 - 92. The GSE District Committee was chaired by Eldon Davidson (Amarillo East) and assisted by Gary Moore (Amarillo West,) Beth Duke (Amarillo West,) Dr. Alice Haynes (Big Spring,) Paul Nabors (Big Spring,) and Mark Swindler (Big Spring.) All but Gary Moore were former GSE members. Two former Youth Exchange Students, Jeff Stuyt and Peter Bergstein, both Rotarians in Lubbock were also on the committee. I have never witnessed such an outstanding and workable combination of Rotarians. They were super.”

“The Korean GSE team arrived in Amarillo on September 30, 1991 and was led by Rotarian Jesu Lee. The five other members of the team were Young-Jun Choi, Hyun-Gu Jung, Jae-Ho Lee, Kwyon-Sub Lee, and Jin-Yong Kim. They spent the month of October touring the District, making stops in Lubbock, Big Spring, and Odessa, then departed for home on October 31st.”

“John Williams (Odessa) was our team leader for the return visit. He had served in the military in Korea and was excited about the exchange. District 3710 in Korea was the location where Lois Rochester, wife of PDG Louis Rochester (Odessa,) had been raised as a child. Her parents were Presbyterian missionaries there. Our group included Daniel R. Linebarger (Midland,) Mark David Hartman (Midland,) Michael D. McMillion (Big Spring,) Ben David Feemster (Big Spring,) and Ernest Glenn Duggan (Midland.) They spent the month of May, 1992 in Korea.”

“The year of 1991-92 in Rotary District 573 was a year of transition. From the beginning on July 1 to year’s end and the celebration at District Conference in Amarillo at the Harvey Hotel it was a wonderful experience. Though both a changing and successful year, we were literally mentally and physically exhausted by the time of District Conference to the extent that even I didn’t care to talk and had little to say, which is next to unbelievable, but I was told that due to that one fact alone, the conference was a very successful one!”

“After some fifty-five club visits and countless thousands of miles of travel we had hoped to unwind. Not so! The District Conference commenced on April 9, 1992 with the arrival of Past General Secretary of R.I. Herbert Pigman and his wife Betty of Ambia, Indiana who was sent by President Saboo as his Special Representative. Herb gave reports on PolioPlus, having served in organizing leadership for this program on five continents. Herb and Betty were most welcome and Herb was familiar with Amarillo as he had cousins in Dalhart. His address was awesome and directly captivating and thrilling.”

“On Thursday the 9th we had a District Governor’s Council meeting. “All Chiefs and no Indians,” and the evening was spent with the PDG’s and their ladies plus Herb and Betty Pigman at the Amarillo Club overlooking Amarillo. Friday the opening plenary session was held at the Tascosa Country Club. PDG Paige Carruth (Canyon) extended the opening welcome, I gave a State of the District address, Cliff Breaud (Lubbock) was introduced as the next District Governor, and Don Williams (Odessa) was presented as District Governor Designee for 1993-94. Herb Pigman spoke at the noon luncheon. His speech was followed an appeal from Miguel Torres of Ojinaga, Mexico Orphanage for “Pop corn cookers” and a “pick me up truck” to help his orphans to sell more popcorn at local schools to support the orphanage. Rotarian Al Abdullah of Dalhart began an appeal and in some ten minutes the fund was raised with the prompting support of Bill Rice (Amarillo West.) “Kernal” Bill Scott (Amarillo West,) a popcorn entrepreneur, assessed the need and purchased the needed equipment and the “right” cooking oil at cost and Miguel Torres was in business. With the help of PDG Louis Rochester (Odessa) and Southwestern Public Service Company manager Roy Holmes (Lubbock,) the popcorn poppers had replaced pans on stoves and the children had two “pick me up” trucks delivering and retrieving them on their popcorn routes.”

“Friday afternoon Director Ralph McLaughlin flew Herb Pigman and Betty over and around the “Texas Grand Canyon” in his Bonanza. Others golfed and shopped. Those who didn’t gathered for a briefing on District projects in the Governor’s suite.”

“Friday evening Bill and Claudette Landess (Amarillo) hosted the Governor’s Banquet. R.I. Director Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) presented Special Representative Herb Pigman who delivered his inspiring speech. Many certificates of achievement were handed out to outstanding clubs within the District with special awards going to L. C. “Chuck” LaBarr (Pampa) - Club President of the Year; Don Dickson (Plainview) - Club of the Year; and Michael Graves (Plainview) and Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock) - Rotarians of the Year. “

“Saturday’s plenary sessions had presentations on Boys’ RYLA by Walter Johnson (Amarillo,) Girls’ RYLA by Larry Johnson (Odessa,) and Tommy Patterson (Southwest Lubbock) and Doyle Moore (Amarillo) discussed the Diabetic Camp and it’s relocation to Ceta Canyon near Canyon. World Community Service projects included a description of the Mexico-Madera club projects at Creel, the orphanages and kindergartens at Ojinaga, and work done with the Tarahumara Indians and Mexican needy by Miguel (The Lion that Roared) Torres, and Father Verplanken (the Bishop’s priest.) Eldon Davidson described the GSE project with Korea, Marilyn Van Petten and G. B. Thompson (Amarillo East) presented information on the Mentoring Program. Claudia Heathington (O’Donnell) discussed their Junior High/Middle School Enhancement Program.”

“PDG Bob Lewis was the speaker at the Motivational Luncheon. His topic was an outgrowth of participating in the Guerrero Eye Clinic in Mexico and was entitled, “Let There Be Light.” That afternoon Dr. Harley Oberhelman (Lubbock) brought us up to date on scholarships and introduced the principal candidate for 1992 - 93 Morgan Dane Boyles (Lubbock) and alternate Carol Spitz. Lee George (Big Spring) reviewed Youth Exchange, PDG Charles Beil spoke on the Rotary Foundation and Conference Resolutions were presented by Bill Countiss (Amarillo West.) “

“We closed the Conference with a dinner dance on Saturday evening at the Tascosa Country Club hosted by the Ken Abbotts (Amarillo) and a Sunday Brunch where Dick Brooks (Amarillo) gave the program. I never recall being so emotionally and physically drained. I was speechless!” (Editor’s note: Does that statement meet the first standard of the Four Way Test?)

“A final reflection: it would be difficult to put on Rotary and then be able to take it off, or stop and reflect to do nothing in Rotary and throughout Rotary without serving. We have been so impressed by the support and loyalty and help afforded to us by the leadership in this Rotary District and it has resulted in our up-most belief in and zeal for this great organization. Any success achieved was for involving those serving and willingly doing Rotary projects and our success was in being allowed to help them. “

- - - - - - - - - - - - - -
During this year Rotary International instigated the “Service Above Self” award, destined to become one of the most prestigious awards that a Rotarian could receive. In January, 1992, Ted Holder (Levelland) was notified by R.I. that he was one of 57 recipients worldwide to receive that distinction. The award was announced at the 1992 District Conference in Amarillo and again at R.I. President Saboo’s International Convention in Orlando, FL., and published in the Rotarian magazine. Rotarians in District 5730 heartily agreed that Ted’s recognition was well deserved.
So ended Governor Cook’s narrative of his year. He did find enough energy to attend the PETS meeting in Dallas in March, host the District Assembly with DGN Cliff Breaud (Lubbock) in Levelland on May 2nd and attend the International Convention in Orlando, Florida on June 14 - 17, 1992 where he served as Master of Ceremonies at the 7:00 a.m. Texas Breakfast on Tuesday morning, June 16th. On July 1st, 1992 he rested.
1992 - 1993
July, 1992 was a busy month. A U.S. District judge in Miami, FL. sentenced General Noriega to 40 years in prison for drug running. Bill Clinton and Al Gore accepted the Democrat Party’s nomination to head their ticket and Ross Perot announced that he would not run for president. The price of hotel rooms in Barcelona, Spain went out of sight as the XXV Summer Olympics began. In the August heat of Houston, George Bush and Dan Quayle were re-nominated by the Republicans as their standard bearers. September was the month that the situation worsened further in the former Yugoslavia. Not many people were thrilled in the western world when Iran announced that China would provide it with a nuclear-power plant. Rotarians visiting Kauai, Hawaii on September 11, 1992 got their money’s worth when hurricane Iniki blew in causing $1.6 billion in damages. Texans chuckled a little bit in October when Ross Perot announced that he was reversing his decision not to run for president of the U.S. Near the end of that month President Bush announced that Vietnam had agreed to turn over all of the documents, photographs, and personal effects that it possessed concerning U.S. personnel missing as a result of the Vietnam war.
November, 1992 began with Bill Clinton and Al Gore winning the election and chess fans noted that Bobby Fisher defeated his old rival Boris Spassky in the 30th game of a nine-week contest. Boris Yeltsin and Britain’s John Major signed a treaty of friendship between their nations. Rotarians who had visited Windsor Castle in England were saddened to learn that the 14th century St. George’s Hall was completely destroyed by fire, but were heartened by the Queen’s statement that it would be repaired and that she would help with the $100 million by paying income taxes.
The U.N. became concerned about the situation in Somalia in December, 1992 that resulted in 1,800 U.S. Marines being sent there, but all was well for the two principal warlords in Mogadishu signed a peace accord. Leaders of Canada, Mexico, and the United States signed the North American Free Trade Agreement and hoped that their legislatures would ratify their efforts. Saddam Hussein tested the U.S. resolve by sending one of his fighter planes into the ‘no fly zone’ in southern Iraq. It didn’t return.
Saddam Hussein wasn’t convinced so to help him understand better, more than 100 U.S., British and French warplanes attacked his missile batteries and radar stations in January, 1993. On the 20th of January William Jefferson Clinton was inaugurated as the 42nd President of the United States. On the 22nd he agreed to withdraw his nomination of Zoe Baird to be his attorney general. On the 25th he named his wife, Hillary, as chair of the Presidential Task Force on National Health Reform. On the 31st, the Dallas Cowboys defeated the Buffalo Bills 52-17 in the Super Bowl.
In February, 1992, six people were killed when a huge bomb exploded in a garage below the World Trade Center in New York City. Janet Reno was sworn in as attorney general of the United States, and the U.N. agreed to get involved in Somalia by sending relief supplies.
April, 1992 news centered on Waco, Texas and the Branch Davidians who had been in a standoff with law enforcement officials for almost two months. On April 22nd the compound burned to the ground in what was described by the F.B.I. as a mass suicide. Tennis fans noted that Monica Seles was hospitalized after being stabbed in the back during a break in a tennis match in Hamburg, Germany.
Remember the seven people dismissed from the White House travel office on May 19, 1993 for financial mismanagement and political corruption? Five of them were reinstated on the 25th after questions were raised about friends and relatives of President Clinton taking over their jobs. In June President Clinton withdrew the nomination of Lani Guinier, law professor, to head the civil rights division of the U.S. Justice Department and 23 U.N. peace keepers were slain in Somalia. Republicans in Texas were heartened by the news that Kay Bailey Hutchinson was elected to complete the senatorial term of Lloyd Bentsen who resigned to become Secretary of the Treasury. The Rotary year ended with a missile attack against Iraq’s intelligence headquarters in Baghdad. In education circles Saddam Hussein would have been designated a slow learner. Some might have questioned why he was in school in the first place.
The world of Rotary was a bright spot on this planet during 1992-1993. Dr. Clifford L. Dochterman of Stockton, California was installed as the President of Rotary International on July 1. President Dochterman was an old friend of Rotarians in District 5730, having acquaintances since his days in Denver and our membership in Zone I. His theme for the year was “Real Happiness is Helping Others.” During his year a ten year drug and alcohol prevention program was adopted. At his Melbourne, Australia International Convention, the 500 millionth child was symbolically immunized against polio. Sixteen “Salutes to the Program of Rotary” were held to recognize and promote Rotary service, and Rotaract celebrated its 25th birthday. Contributions to the Foundation’s Annual Program Fund totaled $44.8 million, PolioPlus received $2.1 million and the Endowment Fund grew to $12.l million. Twelve hundred sixty-two Ambassadorial Scholarships were awarded during President Dochterman’s year. New clubs in Eastern Europe helped increase the number of clubs in Rotary to 26,608 with membership growing to 1,171,348 Rotarians. The Rotary International Convention was held in Melbourne, Australia and was attended by 22,083 Rotarians and guests.
Things continued to go well for Rotary in District 5730. PDG Bob Lewis (Big Spring) was Nominations Chairman in 1990-91 and his committee unanimously selected Dr. Clifford Joseph Breaud to be District Governor for the year 1992-93 and it proved to be a brilliant selection. Governor Breaud was an Orthodontist and a member of the Lubbock Rotary Club. He was reared in Gramercy, LA. and joined the U.S. Army Air Corps in 1940, was trained as a pilot, and flew airplanes during WWII for the Air Corps until 1947. After the war he began his college work at Texas Tech then transferred his studies to Loyola University in New Orleans. During his senior year at Loyola he served as President of Psi Omega, a national dental professional fraternity. He graduated with a degree in Dentistry in 1951 and in November of that year he moved to Lubbock, Texas and began his practice of Orthodontics, a career that spanned four decades. Governor Breaud was a member of all of the professional societies and associations one would expect and served each as president, chairman, or committee head. He was very generous with his time where civic involvement was concerned. Organizations that benefited from his service include the Lubbock Chamber of Commerce, Foundation for Orthodontic Research, Society for Crippled Children, Citizens Traffic Council, Airport Board, P.T.A., Southwest Little League, and Lubbock and Military Bass Associations.
Governor Breaud married Moguyneta (Moggie) Thompson of Lubbock , Texas in 1946. They had two sons, one who was an Orthodontist and one who was deceased. The entire family was heavily involved in bass fishing and snow skiing.
Governor Breaud joined the Lubbock Rotary Club in 1979. He was actively involved in this large club in many capacities and served as its president in 1984-1985. After his presidency he remained active on the District level and began his training for the Governorship in earnest in 1991-92. As District Governor Nominee and with Moggie by his side he attended the Diabetic Camp in June, 1991, both RYLA camps in July, the Zone 5-11 Seminar on October 2-6 in El Paso, and the Foundation Seminar and Paul Harris Dinner in November. March 26-29, 1992 was the PETS meeting in Dallas, then they were off to Kansas City, Missouri for 10 days in April for the Rotary-intensive International Assembly where they met with their 490 fellow incoming governors and almost as many of Rotary’s top worldwide leadership. They attended the District Conference April 9 - 12, 1992 in Amarillo, met their incoming club officers and committee chairs at the District Assembly in Levelland on May 2, then it was on to Big Spring on May 28th to visit R.I. President Saboo. They attended the Rotary International Convention in Orlando, Florida June 14 - 17, 1992. With such a year behind them, and all of the advice they got from PDG’s, DGN Breaud and Moggie were primed to share Rotary in the District.
Every Rotarian that got within 30 miles of Lubbock during Governor Breaud’s year toured the Breedlove Dehydration Plant and the Apple Orchard project. It seems that the germ for this idea came up when Governor Jim Cook and Sue, DGN Breaud and Moggie, and Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock) had lunch in Big Spring when President Saboo dropped by in May, 1992. The topic of dehydration of foods from surpluses within the District’s fruit and vegetable wasted produce came up. Following is a narrative written by PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo) that tells the beginning of Governor Breaud’s enthusiasm for this project.
“Sue and I went to pin the incoming District Governor Dr. Clifford Breaud of the Lubbock Rotary Club on June 30th, 1992. Following the ceremony Cliff took us to the South Plains Food Bank to talk with Ms. Carolyn Lanier, Executive Director. She gave us the ‘Cook’s Tour’ then asked us what Rotary was going to do to feed the hungry of the world and this country. Instead of looking for exits and offering excuses Cliff said, “within three weeks we will have the R.I. personnel here to tell your what they and you can do.” We returned to Cliff’s office, Cliff called Director Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) who said, “let’s meet next Wednesday.” PDRI and Foundation Trustee Jack Forest (Mexia) was called and said he would come. PDG John Tyler (Houston,) R.I. Chairman of the Committee on Hunger for the United States, Canada, and Bermuda arranged his schedule so he could attend our meeting. We talked it over and Director McLaughlin said, “Raise the funds locally and regionally, make a working example, develop the technology and Rotary will join you to replicate this feeding the hungry throughout the world of Rotary.”
The Breedlove Dehydration Plant Board of Directors (Ed. note: PDG Jim Cook, member) raised $6,500,000 from foundations and Rotarians to build a plant that could salvage massive amounts of produce, reduce it to 5% of its volume, and package it in 5 pound bags that could be rehydrated to feed 150 people at less than 2 cents per serving. It worked, distribution of food became worldwide, and many people and agencies were involved.
Governor Breaud continued to pursue this project with great enthusiasm. In discussions with a few PDG’s, Lubbock Rotarians, and the Breedlove staff, an idea for a Rotary District 5730 Apple Orchard was conceived, planned out, and pursued. Dr. George O. Elle (Lubbock) had offered to plant and maintain 1200 apple trees on five acres of the Breedlove farm if Rotary could buy the trees, drill a well, and install a drip irrigation system. An appeal to Rotarians for support was widely publicized during Governor Breaud’s year and District Rotarians found the idea worthy of support. (Ed. note: the rest of this story will be told in Governor Williams’ year, 1993-94.)
Governor Breaud and Moggie commenced their official visits to the 55 clubs in the District in early July, 1992. They took time out to visit both Boys’ RYLA July 5-10, 1992 and Girls’ RYLA July12-17th. The camps were held in New Mexico. Back on the road in the District, Governor Breaud conferred with the following club officers:

During his official visits and throughout his year Governor Breaud emphasized several District projects. One was the Arch Klumph awards. A very ambitious $100,000 had been set as a goal for the Rotary Foundation in the District and this was one of the approaches Governor Breaud used to reach it, and he reached it. He asked Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock) if he could produce a bunch of polished stone bolo ties, maybe 900 or so. Howard said he could. Before the year ended, over one half of the District Rotarians were wearing bolo ties produced by Rotarian Mercer and his wife, Emma Lou, 1500 in all. Many clubs were 100% donors and Plainview was the first club in the District to attain that honor when President David DeBusk presented the Governor with a check on his fourth official visit. Other clubs who were 100% donors in mid year included Greater Big Spring, Levelland, Odessa, Pampa, Amarillo East, Tulia, Southwest Lubbock, Big Spring, Amarillo West, Lubbock, Dimmitt, Levelland, Amarillo, and Snyder. Eleven other clubs made it by year’s end.

Norris Clark (Lubbock) was named as Chairman of the District Tree Project and on November 14, he hosted PDG Forrest Moore of Dallas who held a tree planting seminar in Lubbock. In the later part of March, 1993, 40,000 pots and 40,000 seedlings arrived and Lubbock Rotarians had a seedling-potting big time. As a result of a great deal of work by Norris Clark and his committee, 40,000 seedlings were planted in the District by 17 clubs ranging from Kermit to Perryton.
On October 1 - 4, 1992 Governor Breaud led a large delegation of PDG’s, DGN Don Williams, and their spouses to the Zone 5 - 11 held in Oklahoma City. Training, motivation, and fellowship was the purpose of the meeting and it was under the direction of PDG and RID Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring.)
World Community Service continued big time with a clothing drive for Mexico conducted early in the fall, 1992 and involved a good number of clubs in the District. District Governor Bill De Groot of District 5520 hosted a meeting of those interested in projects in District 4110 in Chihuahua, Mexico and several Rotarians from the District attended the meeting. . It was held at the Inn of the Mountain Gods in Ruidoso October 30 - 31, 1992.
When he wasn’t polishing stones for bolo ties, Rotarians were button-holed by Southwest Lubbock Rotarian Howard Mercer assisting Levelland Rotarian Ted Holder in collecting and delivering 40,000 pounds of clothing, books, medical equipment and supplies to Mexico during the month of December, 1992. Later Howard worked on a similar project with a group in Nigeria. In his spare time he promoted the dehydration plant and apple orchard idea.
PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) chaired the Rotary Foundation Seminar on November 7th at the Lubbock Country Club. Twenty-three clubs were represented at the meeting. The Paul Harris Dinner was held that evening, chaired by Claude Freeman (Lubbock) and his wife. About 80 Rotarians and guests attended the dinner and were treated to a speech by PDG “Sonny” Brown of El Paso. “Sonny” was destined to follow PDG Ralph McLaughlin as a Director of Rotary International.
Governor Breaud recognized that District Committees conducted much of the work accomplished during every Rotary year and he selected the following Rotarians to assist him in the areas indicated: C. David Cobb (Lubbock) - District Secretary; Brax Wright (Lubbock) - District Treasurer; Jim Douglass (Lubbock) - District Conference; PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West) - Nominations; Ron Bailey (Southwest Lubbock) - Free Enterprise; PDG Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) - PolioPlus; Tommy Patterson (Southwest Lubbock) - Diabetic Camp and Community Service; Bob Nash (Lubbock) and Margaret Simon (Lubbock) - District Public Relations; PDG J. D. Cage (Muleshoe) - Extension; Lon Moser (Amarillo West) - Resolutions; W. L. Goble (Levelland) - District Liability Insurance; Walter Johnson (Amarillo) - Boys’ RYLA; Larry Johnson (Odessa) - Girls’ RYLA; PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) - Rotary Foundation; Eldon Davidson (Amarillo East) - Group Study Exchange; Dr. Harley Oberhelman and Kenneth L. Ketner (Lubbock) - Scholarships; PDG Bob Lewis (Big Spring) - Development, Planned, and Annual Giving; PDG Edward Self (Plainview) - Paul Harris Fellows; PDG Burnett Roberts (Levelland) - Special Matching Grants; Don Patterson (Amarillo West) - Charitable Trusts; PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West) - Arch Klumph Awards; PDG Bill Hubbs (Pecos) - Club Service; PDG Davis Armistead (Membership Development); Jack Sherrod (Levelland) - Club Bulletins; Dudley Faver (Lubbock) - Rotary Information; PDG Jack Selby (Lubbock) Attendance; David Gibson (Lubbock) - Vocational Service; Scott Foster (Denver City) - Interact and Rotaract; PDG Louis Rochester (Odessa) - International Service; Ted Holder (Levelland) - World Community Service; and Lee George (Big Spring) - Youth Exchange.
Governor Breaud was quite complimentary of the work done by his Area Representatives. They included L. C. “Chuck” LaBarr (Pampa,) Robert Holland (Perryton,) Jack Thompson (Dimmitt,) Michael Graves (Plainview,) Phelps Blume (Levelland,) Fred Chesser (Amarillo East,) Sammy Biggers (Lubbock,) Steve Sanders (Tahoka,) William Black (Midland,) John Thomas (Snyder,) Lynn F. Smallwood (Pecos,) and Larry Morris (Andrews.)
 Pampa Rotarians saw an opportunity for a World Community Service project that was reported by Club P.R. Chairman Jeff Boyd. When club president Dr. Joe Lowry heard that a Pampa corporation, IRI International, was shipping a large quantity of oil well equipment to Siberia, he asked Vic Raymond, president of IRI if there would be any extra space in the cargo containers. When he found that space was available medical equipment from Coronado Hospital and retired physician Dr. Joe Donaldson was collected, trucked to Houston, loaded on a shipping container, and sent to a hospital at Nizhnevartvsk in western Siberia.
Plainview club president David DeBusk reported that his club still had their Mexico connection. One of their World Community Service projects that year was to provide the city of Parrel, Mexico with an ambulance that would serve their population of over 150,000 people.
The visiting Group Study Exchange Team from South Africa arrived in Lubbock on March 31, 1993. They were greeted by Pieter Bergstein, Jeff Stuyt, and Governor Breaud at the airport. The team leader was Rotarian Rob Butterwort, a minister from Bloemfontein. He was accompanied by Phil Barnard (cattle rancher,) Nigel Payne (accountant,) Andre Joubert (doctor,) Keith Wattrus (political analysis,) and Gillian Edwards (teacher.) Their exchange visit was coordinated by the Rotary clubs in Lubbock, Big Spring, Midland, and Amarillo. The team departed for their homes in South Africa on May 1, 1993.
The 35th Annual District Conference was held April 22 - 24, 1993 in Lubbock and was hosted by the four Lubbock Rotary Clubs. Jim Douglass was the conference chairman and coordinated the efforts of the clubs’ representatives who attended to the myriad details of this undertaking. Committee members included Sammy Biggers, Susan Bowen, Randy Christian, Ken Condray, Bob Craig, Jerry Griffin, Greg Jones, Chuck Key, Eric McDonald, Kevin McMahon, Tommy Patterson, Joe Rousseau, Scott Shellhase, Jim Shute, Karen Smith, Bob Strange, Bill Tarro, Judy Vance, Stan Weaver, and Marjan Wilkins.
Governor Breaud opened the conference on April 22 with a black tie dinner attended by the PDG’s, the R. I. Special Representative, and their spouses. DGN Don Williams presided at a dinner for club Presidents Elect and their spouses. Friday morning was devoted to sports activities and tours. The noon All Conference Luncheon featured R. I. President Cliff Dochterman’s Special Representative to the conference PDG William L. Plunkett of the Rotary Club of Los Angeles, California and District 5280. Bill, who was accompanied by his wife, Harriett, charmed the audience and proved to be an outstanding resource for the conference. Friday afternoon was devoted to Governor Breaud’s State of the District address, a report on legislation by PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring,) and the introduction of the District Governor Designee (1994 - 95) L. C. “Chuck” LaBarr (Pampa.) That evening a Shrimp Boil was held at the National Guard Armory, hosted by the Greater Lubbock club, and certainly lived up to Governor Breaud’s conference theme “The Wild, Wild, Fest.”
 Saturday was another big day and it began with Eldon Davidson’s (Amarillo East) introduction of the members of the Group Study Exchange Team from South Africa. The GSE team that visited Korea from District 5730 were then presented and reported on their experiences. The Motivational Luncheon was held in the Atrium of the Lubbock Plaza and Mayor David R. Langston (Lubbock) proved to be a dynamic speaker. Saturday afternoon was devoted to Rotary Information and District Projects and included presentations on the Rotary Foundation (PDG Charles Beil, Big Spring,) Vocational Service (David Gibson, Lubbock,) Paul Harris Fellow (PDG Bill Hubbs, Pecos,) World Community Service (Ted Holder, Levelland,) Youth Exchange (Lee George, Big Spring,) Ambassadorial Scholarships (Dr. Harley Oberhelman, Lubbock,) Boys’ RYLA (Walter Johnson, Amarillo,) Girls’ RYLA (Sherri Sparks (Big Spring,) Diabetic Camp (Tommy Patterson, Southwest Lubbock), Club Bulletins (Jack Sherrod, Levelland,) and Necrology (Jim Shute, Greater Lubbock.)
The Governor’s Awards Banquet was a festive affair and selection committees had a difficult chore in trying to decide who should be cited for what, for many clubs and individual Rotarians were active in practicing Service Above Self. Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock) was ultimately named Rotarian of the Year (World Community Service projects with Mexico & Nigeria, 1500 bolo ties, promotion of Breelove dehydration plant.) Best Bulletin Awards went to Lubbock (large clubs,) Borger (medium sized clubs,) and Amarillo East (small clubs.) The Outstanding Club committee threw in the towel and named four clubs instead of one that met the rigorous criteria. President Doris Reding accepted the award for Levelland, President Stan Weaver for Greater Lubbock, President Curtis Saylor for Odessa, and President David DeBusk for Plainview.
A week after the District Conference about 60% of club presidents elect, Governor Breaud, DGN Don Williams, DGD Chuck LaBarr and several other District leaders who were invited to be on the faculty traveled to Dallas for the annual President Elect Training Seminar (PETS). The three day meeting which was devoted exclusively to training club presidents was held at the DFW Hyatt April 30 - May 2, 1993. The meeting was designated as mandatory for incoming club presidents in District 5730 by-laws but 100% participation had never been achieved despite vigorous promotion by District Governors.
The District Assembly was held in Plainview May 15, 1993 and was hosted by club president David DeBusk and other member of the Plainview Rotary Club. Governor Breaud convened the meeting which was designed to acquaint presidents elect, officers, and committee chairs with District 5730 and their duties within their clubs. DGN Don Williams (Odessa,) organized the meeting and was assisted by DGD Chuck LaBarr (Pampa,) and a host of other District leaders who participated in the program.
The District GSE Committee, chaired by Eldon Davidson (Amarillo East) selected the following business and professional representatives to compose the GSE team: PDG Bob Lewis (Big Spring) was the Rotarian team leader; Philip Hamilton, newspaper columnist, was sponsored by Plainview; Lynn A. Simpson, biologist, was sponsored by Big Spring; Gary Shanks, newspaper columnist, was sponsored by Greater Big Spring; Rhonda Fowler, college counselor was sponsored by Big Spring; and Elizabeth Nelson, lawyer, was sponsored by Lubbock. The outbound portion of the District’s Group Study Exchange departed for District 9320 in South Africa on May 18, 1993. Twelve Rotary clubs served as hosts for the group. Six very tired GSE members arrived back in District 5730 on June 23, 1993 using superlatives by the dozens to describe their adventure.
The Rotary International Convention was held in Melbourne, Australia May 23 - 27, 1993. DGN Don Williams and Rita (Odessa,) DGD Chuck LaBarr and Faye (Pampa), RI Director Ralph McLaughlin and Billye (Big Spring,) and others from the District journeyed down under for the adventure. Director Ralph McLaughlin helped host the Texas Breakfast, an always popular event at International Conventions.

Near the end of his year Governor Breaud reflected on the things accomplished by Rotarians during his year. The Foundation goal of $100,000 had been exceeded, enthusiasm for the dehydration plant and apple orchard projects in Lubbock was growing, the Group Study Exchange and Youth Exchange programs were working well, World Community Service projects were being successfully carried out by several clubs, the RYLA and Diabetic Camps were outstanding, and he and Moggie had made many, many new friends and experienced one of the most rewarding years of their lives. On June 23, 1993 Governor Breaud and Moggie traveled to Odessa to “change the guard.” His sly grin was not unnoticed as he pinned Don Williams (Odessa) as his replacement.


CHAPTER IX

Rotary Saves the World

With PolioPlus

1993 - 1994

This Rotary year started off with President Clinton fulfilling a campaign promise by easing the ban on homosexuals serving in the military, asking them to be discreet about their behavior. Robert V. Rota, postmaster of the U.S. House of Representatives plead guilty to helping U.S. House members in obtaining illegal funds from the House Post Office during his tenure, and Vincent W. Foster, Jr., deputy White House counsel was found dead in northern Virginia, an apparent suicide.

Things were only so-so internationally. Israel went after the pro-Iranian group Hezbollah in Southern Lebanon in retaliation for rocket attacks, and Somalia continued to be a sore spot when four American soldiers were killed in August. U.S. jets bombed an Iraqi site after the installation fired upon U. S. planes. Optimism prevailed when Yasir Arafat of the P.L.O. announced that Israel had a right to exist and Yitzhak Rabin recognized the P.L.O. as the sole representative of the Palestinian people but factions in the Middle East were unhappy about that.

In September space fans were saddened when the Mars Observer was presumed to be lost, but cheers rang out when the Clinton administration announced its plan for “reinventing government” so as to improve government efficiency and reduce costs. Much gnashing of teeth occurred when President Clinton unveiled his program for reforming the nation’s health system.

Boris Yeltsin faced an uprising by rebellious members of Parliament and killed 125 persons while showing them who was boss. President Clinton ordered 15,000 reinforcements for troops in Somalia after 12 more U.S. soldiers were killed in October. The calendar year ended with the U.S. space shuttle Endeavor repairing the Hubble Space Telescope, the daughter of Cuba’s Fidel Castro defecting to the U.S., and President Clinton announcing that his lawyers would give investigators all documents related to his investment in the Whitewater Land Corporation.

In January, 1994 one era ended when Lawrence Walsh released the final report on the Iran-contra affair that beset the Reagan administration, and another began when an inquiry was started into the Whitewater affair, Arkansas real-estate and financial dealings of President and Mrs. Clinton. Kay Bailey Hutchinson, Republican Senator from Texas was found not guilty by a state court of misusing state funds and personnel for politician purposes.

In March, four Arab defendants were found guilt on all counts in the February, 1993 bombing of the World Trade Center in New York City, and Tanya Harding plead guilty to a conspiracy charge arising from an assault against skater Nancy Kerrigan. The movie Schindler’s List won the Oscar for the year’s best picture, and the U.S. pulled out of Somalia ending its mission there.

News was reported in April and May that saddened some and elated other. Two U.S. Army helicopters were shot down in northern Iraq by U.S. Air Force F-15C warplanes killing 26 people, and former President Richard M. Nixon died at the age of 81. Nelson Mandela claimed victory in South Africa’s first all-race election and was inaugurated as president on May 10th. In Singapore, Michael Fay, an 18 year old U.S. citizen was caned after being convicted of vandalism, and Paula Corbin Jones, a former state employee in Arkansas, filed a federal lawsuit accusing President Clinton of sexual harassment when he was governor of Arkansas. Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis died of cancer at the age of 64, and Dan Rostenkowski (D-IL) stepped down as chairman of the House Ways and Means Committee after being indicted on 17 felony counts of fraud, embezzlement, and obstruction of justice.

The World War II generation paused on June 6, 1994 to remember the D-Day invasion of France while heads of state gathered in Normandy, France to mark the 50th anniversary of the massive assault that resulted in Allied forces regaining control of Western Europe from Nazi Germany. The Bosnian Muslim-Croat federation and the Bosnian Serbs signed another short-lived agreement to cease fighting, and the American news media was captivated when O.J. Simpson was arrested on June 17, 1994 and charged with murdering his wife and a male friend of hers.

One of the things that the world needed badly was exactly what it got through the efforts of thousands upon thousands of Rotarians. PolioPlus, Rotary’s premier service project that was announced in 1985, received immense support from club members. Total PolioPlus funds contributed since its beginning reached $247 million during the Rotary year. In 1994 the Western Hemisphere was declared polio-free and two years later that list had grown to 150 nations. The year 2000 was set as the date for global polio eradication and 2005, Rotary’s 100th Anniversary, was the established time that Rotarians could celebrate the certification of a world without polio.

Rotary was a major player in the development of a world partnership that included the World Health Organization, UNICEF, and the U.S. Centers for Disease Control and Prevention to achieve a common goal of polio eradication. District 5730 was a major player in Rotary’s PolioPlus vision. Consider the following words written by PRID Ralph McLaughlin:

“This, the largest humanitarian effort ever attempted by private philanthropy, just could not have happened without the tremendous acceptance of the concept by individual Rotarians. Their willingness to open their purses for the children of the world will go down in history as Rotary’s finest hour.”

 “Rotarians in different parts of the world were called on to perform myriad activities to assist in the effort and assure that Rotary reached its goal of complete elimination of polio throughout the entire world by the year 2005. In District 5730 and indeed - all of Texas - Rotarians were unable to assist the State Health Department. State law actually precluded volunteer workers from administering vaccines to children. Having seen firsthand the enormous enthusiasm generated when Rotarians planned and implemented publicity for National Polio Immunization Days in the Philippines and were subsequently allowed to participate in administering the vaccines - it was a great disappointment to me personally that Rotarians in this District were denied this opportunity.”

“Of course, the campaign has been effective in Texas. We have not had a reported case of Polio in several years even though our vaccination rate falls far short of what they have accomplished in the Philippines. My lament is that individual Rotarians did not share the thrill of actually administering the vaccine that Billye and I enjoyed along with the Rotarians in Manila. I am sorry too, that Rotary, after funding the campaign, was denied the name recognition due us. I’m afraid that there are many Rotarians, particularly new ones, that will never realize the key role that Rotary had in this endeavor.”

“Make no mistake, when the world is polio-free it will be because Rotarians made it happen, and the Rotarians of this district can be particularly proud of their contributions.” (Ed. Note: emphases are mine.)

 Rotarians continued to pursue the Objective of Rotary and leading that effort was Robert Barth of Aarau, Switzerland who was installed as President of Rotary International on July 1, 1993. President Barth’s theme for the year was “Believe In What You Do--Do What You Believe In.” Two pilot programs were adopted as official R.I. programs: Preserve Planet Earth and Rotary Volunteers. Eight outstanding service projects in different parts of the world were recognized and designated as “Rotary at Its Best.” Herb Pigman, recent President’s Special Representative to the 5730 District Conference, was elected for a second term as R.I. general secretary. During this year contributions to the Rotary Foundation Annual Programs Fund totaled $48.9 million and the Permanent Fund grew to $17.8 million. Total PolioPlus funds contributed since its beginning in 1988 reached $247 million. One thousand three hundred twenty-seven Ambassadorial Scholarships were awarded. The number of clubs in Rotary rose to 27,026 and had 1,190,102 members at the end of President Barth’s year. He held his International Convention in Taipei, Taiwan, China and 31,161 Rotarians and guests were in attendance.

The long, long tradition of selecting truly outstanding Rotarians to provide leadership for the programs in the District continued unabated. Donivan R. Williams was pinned as District Governor effective July 1, 1993. Governor Williams was a 31 year member of the Rotary club of Odessa with perfect attendance during that time. He served his club as president in 1973 - 1974, became a Paul Harris Fellow the same year, and a Benefactor of the Rotary Foundation in 1989. He was active in the District in many capacities, freely offering his time, expertise, and a smile when asked to serve. He co-chaired a District Conference, chaired the Hospitality Committee at another, attended several International Conventions, and participated in a tour of Scotland and England under the auspices of a London Rotary Club in 1978.

Governor Williams was born in Rockville, Indiana, attended the University of Wyoming and arrived in Odessa in 1948. He was president of Western Tank Company and Shamrock Steel Sales. His business affiliations included the Odessa Chamber of Commerce (board member, president, Odessa’s Outstanding Citizen 1979, Volunteer of the Year 1992,) Small Business Administration (District Advisory Council,) Better Business Bureau (board member,) and Texas Manufacturers Association (State Director.)

He was generous with his time in many civic organizations including the United Way of Odessa (member of the board, executive committee, campaign chairman, president,) Salvation Army (chairman, advisory board,) The Oasis Foundation (board member, V.P.,) Odessa Civic Concert Association (board member, president,) Permian Playhouse (board member,) Odessa Knife and Fork Club (president,) and the list goes on. Governor Williams received enough awards to fill three walls in a very large office.

Governor Williams married Rita D. Roberts and they raised two sons. Rita was a Paul Harris Fellow and Benefactor. Son Michael of Austin was a Paul Harris Fellow and president elect of his Rotary Club in Austin. They were members of the First Presbyterian Church of Odessa where Don served as elder, teacher and choir member.

As District Governor Nominee 1992-93 Don and Rita traveled extensively to learn more about the governorship. Visits were made to the Diabetic Camp in June, both RYLA camps in July, the three day Zone 5-11 meeting held in Oklahoma City in October, and the Foundation Seminar and Paul Harris Dinner in Lubbock. In the spring of 1993 the 10 day Rotary International Assembly was held in Anaheim, California where DGN Williams took his baptism in Rotary training along with the 501 fellow DGNs then he was off to the 3 day President-Elect Training Seminar (PETS) in Dallas, the 4 day District Conference held in Lubbock in April, the District Assembly where he met with his incoming club officers in Plainview, and then journeyed to Melbourne, Australia to attend the 5 day R. I. Convention. During his year he had many meetings and conversations with Governor Breaud (Lubbock) and felt ready to take the reins when his turn came.

The Governor’s pin was passed from PDG Cliff Breaud to Governor Williams in late June and it became official on July 1, 1993. Official visits to the 55 clubs in the District began immediately with the intent of finishing them before Labor Day. Governor Williams and Rita also paid visits to the Diabetic Camp, Boys’ RYLA held near Taos June 27 - July 2, and Girls’ RYLA held at the same location July 11 - 17. Governor Williams had met with about two-thirds of the clubs when he issued his second newsletter (September) and in it he demonstrated agreement with other PDG’s when he said, “It is a long way from here to there in Rotary in District 5730.” (The Governor logged almost 10,000 miles on his car during his first four months.) During his travels three things were stressed while making his official visits: securing and retaining members, participation in local and Rotary youth programs, and support for and participation in the programs of the Rotary Foundation. Governor Williams was pleased with the officers he met on his rounds and they included:
