The Zone 5 - 11 meeting was held in Lafayette, Louisiana on Sept. 29 - Oct. 2, 1993. Governor Williams and Rita, with DGN Chuck LaBarr (Pampa) and Faye led a large group of PDG’s and their spouses to the training and motivational meeting. The R.I. Director for these two Zones Richard E. Burnett (Overland Park, Kansas) was in charge and called on top Rotary leadership for presentations regarding the status and direction of Rotary.

Jack Wiggins, president of the Borger Rotary Club, announced in October, 1993 that R. I. had approved their request for a matching grant equal to the $1,000 raised by Borger club members. The $2,000 was used to provide school books and fans for the Benito Juarez Orphanage school in Reynosa, Mexico. The Rotary Club of Reynosa helped coordinate the project locally.

An analysis from Rotary International concerning general giving to the Rotary Foundation during the year 1992-93 reported that contributions totaling over $100,000 were received from 37 clubs in the District. The Governor set his sights on the 18 clubs that chose not to support the Foundation, a situation he hoped would not recur during his year.

The Rotary Foundation Trustees notified Timothy Edward Walker of Midland that he had been selected for an Ambassadorial Scholarship good for a year’s study at the University of St. Andrews in Scotland (District 1010) in 1994-95. Mr. Walker was sponsored by the Midland Rotary Club.

Governor Williams reasoned that if the programs of Rotary in District 5730 were to be accomplished he would need the help of dedicated and able Rotarians. With that in mind he appointed the following committee chairs: Thomas Petersen (Odessa) - District Secretary; Peggy Dean (Odessa) - Treasurer and District Conference Co-Chair; Don Blair (Odessa) - District Conference; PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock) - Nominations; Ron Bailey (Lubbock) - Free Enterprise; Tommy Patterson (Southwest Lubbock) - Diabetic Camp; Gary Watkins (Odessa) - Resolutions; Margaret Simon (Lubbock) - Public Relations; PDG J. D. Cage (Muleshoe) - Extension; W. L. Goble (Levelland) - District Liability Insurance; Walter Johnson (Amarillo) - Boys’ RYLA; Dr. Cheri T. Sparks (Big Spring) - Girls’ RYLA; PDG Edward Self (Plainview) - Rotary Foundation; Beth Duke (Amarillo West) - Group Study Exchange; Dr. Kenneth L. Ketner (Lubbock) - Scholarships; PDRI Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) - PolioPlus; PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West) - Special Matching Grants; PDG Bob Lewis (Big Spring) - Endowment/Planned/Annual Giving/Major Gifts; Dudley Faver (Lubbock) - Rotary Information; PDG Bill Hubbs (Pecos) - Club Service; PDG Davis Armistead (Lubbock) - Membership Development; PDG Jack Selby (Lubbock) - Attendance; Jack Sherrod and Doris Kennedy (Levelland) - Club Bulletins; Michael Tandy (Midland) - Vocational Service; Curtis Saylor (Odessa) - Community Service; Robert Taylor (Lubbock) - Interact and Rotaract; PDG Louis Rochester (Odessa) - International Service; Ted Holder (Levelland) - World Community Service; PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) - Friendship Exchange; Lee George (Big Spring) - Youth Exchange; and Mike Graves (Plainview) - World Fellowship Activities which was a new District Committee.

Governor’s Area Representatives included Curt Beck (Pampa,) Doug Kile (Perryton,) Paul Garcia (Dimmitt,) David DeBusk (Plainview,) Buford A. Duff (Levelland,) Fred Chesser (Amarillo East,) Sammy Biggers (Lubbock,) Travis LaGrone (Lamesa,) Larry Johnson (Odessa,) Tim Fambrough (Sweetwater,) Dan Gibbs (Monahans,) and James Satterwhite (Seminole.)

November, 1993 was a busy month for Rotarians. The Paul Harris Dinner was held in Amarillo Nov. 12 and was hosted by the four Rotary Clubs there. Using CompuServe’s Rotary Forum Doris Moore (Amarillo,) member of the planning committee, secured 5 crates of apples from Herman teVelde, member of the Sunnyside Daybreak Rotary Club of Sunnyside, Washington (District 5060) that were used as decorations and served two additional purposes: they stressed the need for the District’s involvement in the Apple Orchard project in Lubbock and they were auctioned off with proceeds going to the Foundation. The project appeared in the April, 1994 issue of The Rotarian. The Rotary Foundation Seminar was held in Amarillo the next day and was chaired by PDG Edward Self (Plainview.)

PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) was busy during the year spreading information about his newest District Committee assignment, Friendship Exchange. PDG Beil reported that interest had been expressed by Districts in England, New Zealand, Chile, Scandinavia, and South Africa. The first one was scheduled with District 1070 in England during 1994-95.
Rotarians from the District journeyed to Dallas on November 16, 1993 to visit with R.I. President Bob Barth (Switzerland). President Barth was in town to recognize the Rota Tree project chaired by PDG Forrest Moore (Dallas,) and designate it as one of eight “Rotary At Its Best” projects worldwide. Readers will recall that PDG Moore held a seminar in Lubbock the previous year and District 5730 took part in this project by planting 40,000 seedlings throughout the District. A large Inter-city Banquet was held at the South Fork Ranch that evening and it was a gala.

On November 19-20, PDRI Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) attended a PolioPlus meeting in Chicago where improvement in immunization levels of children under age 2 living in the United States was the topic. This followed a meeting he attended in Austin on Oct. 20th representing Rotary at the Texas Health Department’s “Shots Across Texas Coalition.” Doing their part Big Spring Rotarians set up an immunization clinic of the first order with help from the local medical community, but when the day came someone in the TDH felt their turf was being infringed upon and shut the project down. There were better terms than “incensed” that could be used to describe the club’s initial reaction but after a couple of phone calls the “turf protector” became exceedingly enthusiastic about the project. Throughout the year PDRI McLaughlin, Governor Williams and other Rotarians vigorously promoted the idea that Rotary Clubs should participate in “Shots Across Texas” by organizing immunization clinics locally to improve Texas’ poor standing in records of young children immunized.

Kerry Denise Phillips was enrolled at the University of Vienna, Austria and reported that all was going well. Kerry was selected as a recipient of a District 5730 Graduate Scholarship, graduated from Texas Tech in 1993 and represented the District with ability as an ambassador of goodwill.

Ted Holder (Levelland) reported on the current year’s District World Community Service project with Mexico, the third one. Clubs in the District that helped on this included Plainview (400 school desks,) Lockney (16 hospital beds, tables, and cabinets,) Odessa (a huge load of equipment,) Levelland (X-ray machine, 7 examination tables, several beds, baby warmers, respirators, anesthesia machines,) Lubbock (5 hospital beds,) and 3,400 tooth brushes from Americares in Conn. Howard Mercer arranged with Wal-Mart in Plainview for two large trucks to transport the loads to Mexico. They departed Levelland on Nov. 19th and got as far as Presidio where off loading was necessary due to paper work problems and border guards. It was hoped that delivery could be made on Nov. 29th to six clinics in four towns and four schools in two other towns.

In late December, 1993, Dr. Ken Ketner (Lubbock,) District Scholarship Chairman, announced the arrival of graduate student Jaesung (Jason) Sim at Texas Tech. Jason was the recipient of a Rotary Ambassadorial Scholarship, was sponsored by the Rotary Club of Iri, District 3670, Korea and planned to pursue a degree in Information Systems Technology.

Governor Williams reported that contributions to the Rotary Foundation in The District July 1 - Nov. 30, 1993 totaled $19,335.96 from 24 clubs. He urged clubs officers to strive for Arch Klumph Award donors and funds from other sources. During that same period of time the Governor reported that District membership had risen from 2,539 to 2,571, a gain of 32 members.

Beth Duke (Amarillo West,) District Group Study Exchange Chair, reported in January, 1994 that her committee had selected David Hester (Lubbock) to be the Rotarian team leader and Jerry Vestal (Snyder) as alternate for the GSE visit to District 4560 in Brazil during the Spring, 1994. She listed the names of the four team members who were chosen from 22 applicants on Feb. 19th who would compose the District 5730 team and they were: Dave Kemp (Amarillo attorney,) Valerie Job (Lubbock teacher,) Roy Wilson (Lubbock teacher,) and Darla Scarrow (Lubbock nurse.) Alternates chosen were Pete Ruiz (Big Spring,) Janice Green (Big Spring,) and Ben Robles (Lubbock.) Beth Duke also stated that those selected would receive five days of language training in Portuguese before departing for Brazil on May 25th.

Beth Duke said that the team from District 4560, Brazil, would arrive in Odessa on April 8th, visit the District Conference, and spend the next 5 weeks in Odessa, Lubbock, Plainview, and Amarillo, departing for home on May 8th, 1994. The Brazilian team leader was Rotarian Wander Batista Da Costa, a cardiologist from the Formiga Rotary Club. He was accompanied by Nivia Da Fonseca Ferreira (biochemist,) Claudio Rodriques Duarte (teacher,) Sislene Machado Alves Vasconcelos (teacher,) and Marcia Maria Silveira (small business owner.)

Speaking of selecting people, PDRI Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) was elected by Zone 5 club presidents to be a member of the 1994 Nominating Committee for the President of Rotary International. He was also elected to be District 5730’s representative to the 1995 Council on Legislation to be held in Caracas, Venezuela. PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock,) District Nominating Chair announced that Rotarian Doyle Moore (Amarillo) was that committee’s selection to serve as District Governor for the year 1995-96.

Governor Williams convened the 36th District Conference at the Holiday Inn Centre in Odessa on April 7, 1994. The Conference was a joint effort by the three Rotary Clubs in Odessa and was chaired by Don Blair and Peggy Dean. Others involved on the Conference Committee included Bruce Troy (All Faith Service,) Chuck Hornung (Audio & Video,) Jeanette Bennett (Awards,) Marilyn Matthews (Budget,) Dr. Ed Schmidt (Bulletins,) Joan Johnson and Larry Johnson (Decorations,) Keith Spradlin (Exhibits,) Susan Brown and Carol Morgan (Friday Night Leisure,) Byron Bartley (Governor’s Banquet,) Neal Marshall (Housing,) Sheri Norton (Family Activities,) Don Shinn (Music,) Mike Barker (Promotion & Attendance,) Dick and Laura Sivalls and John and Stephanie Latirner (Reception & Hospitality,) Stan Smith (Youth Exchange,) Paul Ahrens (Registration,) Gary Watkins (Resolutions & Credentials,) Mark Donaldson (Sergeant at Arms,) Jim Butler (Sports,) Charlie Taylor (Transportation,) Craig Van Amburgh (Program,) and PDG Louis Rochester (Past District Governor’s Banquet.) They left no stone unturned in their preparation.

Governor Williams met on Thursday afternoon with his District Advisory Committee to share ideas, consider proposals, and chart the future course of programs in the District. That evening at the PDG’s Dinner he introduced the President’s Special Representative PDG Clinton D. Hamilton and his wife Margaret from Plantation, Florida. PDG Hamilton was associated with Broward County Community College, was active in Rotary on all levels, and possessed all of the Rotary credentials one would expect of a Special Representative.

The Governor gave his State of the District address on Friday April 8th, Griffin Jones of Odessa was the featured speaker at the luncheon, sports and tours were conducted Friday afternoon, and “A Night in the Ol’ West” was filled with dinner and dancing that evening.

Saturday was devoted to the programs of Rotary on the club, district, and international levels. Beth Duke (Amarillo West) presented the visiting Group Study Exchange Team from District 4560 in Brazil and the outbound team from District 5730 about to depart for Brazil. Tommy Patterson (Southwest Lubbock) brought everyone up to date on the Diabetic Camp and Ted Holder (Levelland) spoke of the many efforts of clubs in the District concerning World Community Service projects with Mexico. Cheri Sparks (Big Spring) discussed Girls’ RYLA and Walter Johnson (Amarillo) described Boys’ RYLA. Ken Ketner (Lubbock) presented information on District Scholarship Awards. All speakers that morning urged club participation in these programs.

The noon Motivational Luncheon was a double treat. The Satin Strings, a large orchestra group from Permian High School in Odessa, walked through the tables of dining Rotarians and guests during the meal and held the group in fascination with their music. After a standing ovation, the crowd was then treated to a speech by Special Representative Clinton Hamilton who described the internationallity of Rotary and the work and theme of R.I. President Bob Barth.

Saturday afternoon Rotarians were provided information on the Rotary Foundation by PDG Edward Self (Plainview.) PDG Self included in his presentation information on the awarding of an engraved crystal to Ray J. Diekemper, Jr. (Lubbock) for his major gift ($10,000 or more) to the Rotary Foundation. Gary Watkins (Odessa) enumerated opportunities awaiting in Vocational Service. Rotarians then met the visiting Youth Exchange students in the District and learned more about that program from Lee George (Big Spring,) got ideas on club bulletins from Ed Schmidt (Greater Odessa,) and adopted three resolutions citing work done by the Conference Committee, Governor Don Williams and Rita, and Special Representative Clinton Hamilton and Margaret. The Governor’s Banquet was held that evening with presentations made by PDG Hamilton and Governor Williams. Food and fellowship were supreme and the Conference closed on a high note that evening, April 9, 1994.

Several awards were presented during the Conference. A crystal engraved with his name went to PDRI Ralph McLaughlin for service and a major gift ($10,000 or more) to the Rotary Foundation. PDRI McLaughlin was the second Rotarian in the District to receive the crystal award. The third crystal award for a major gift to the Foundation went to Governor Donivan R. Williams. The Rotary Foundation Citation for Meritorious Service went to PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock) for service to the Foundation; PDG Louis Rochester (Odessa) was recognized as Rotarian of the Year for his long history of service to Rotary; Best Club Bulletin - large clubs, went to Lubbock Southwest’s “Keyway;” the medium clubs award went to Metropolitan Lubbock’s “Rotary Banner;” and the small clubs winner was Amarillo East’s “The Easterner.” Four clubs were presented special plaques for exemplifying Service Above Self: Amarillo South, Levelland, Greater Odessa, and Pampa.

Governor Williams reported that 350 Rotarians and guests registered for the Conference and represented 32 of the 55 clubs in the District.

The Texas version of the President-Elect Training Seminar (PETS) was held in Dallas on April 21 - 24, 1994. Forty-four of the 55 incoming club president from District 5730 were there and received comprehensive training about their forthcoming year. Governor Williams, DGN Chuck LaBarr, and several PDG’s were invited to attend and take part in the program.

PETS was followed on April 30th by the District Assembly held in Levelland and conducted by DGN Chuck LaBarr (Pampa.) The program included presentations of Rotary information by district leaders and chairs of district committees and was designed to assist the incoming officers and club chairs in meeting their Rotary responsibilities. Each year approximately 20 - 25 Rotarians prepared presentations for the Assembly and covered vital information about clubs, district projects, and Rotary International . Thirty-four of the District’s 55 clubs were represented by 70 Rotarians who registered for the Assembly.

The Apple Orchard project continued to take shape. Lubbock Rotarians were promoting the idea, PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West) was working on a Matching Grant from R.I. for funding, the District Advisory Committee approved the project on April 7th, and Dr. George O. Elle (Lubbock) got it underway in late spring. The initial phase was to plant 1200 trees on 5 acres of land made available by the Breedlove Dehydration Plant. Rotarian Elle said that he would strip the blossoms from the trees during the first two years to promote tree growth and harvest apples the third year, expecting 20-30 pounds per tree with increases to 120-150 pounds per tree by the 10th year. Governor Williams announced that “official” recognition of the project was scheduled for August 27, 1994 at the orchard site in Lubbock.

Scholarship Chairman Kenneth Ketner (Lubbock) announced the selection of two Graduate Ambassadorial Scholarship awardees in June, 1994. Dawn Lee Dale, a 1994 graduate of Texas Tech, planned to study music in Europe. Nikki Dee Harris, also a 1994 graduate of Texas Tech, planned to study Spanish and Latin American Studies in Central or South America. Their studies were conducted in the 1995-96 academic year. The two scholarships awarded that year, each valued at $21,500, were due to the substantial contributions Rotarians made to the Rotary Foundation in 1992-93. Under the Share Program of the Foundation 60% of contributions were credited to the District for use in funding scholarships and Group Study Exchange programs.

The six Rotary Clubs of Midland and Odessa undertook a cooperative project of building a one acre “Rotary Park” at the Midland-Odessa airport. Its location was to be adjacent to the Vietnam Memorial and convenient for visitor’s use during tours of the Confederate Air Force Museum. Cost of the project was estimated to be $90,000. The amount of $5,000 was contributed from funds available as surplus from the April District Conference at Odessa. An additional surplus was turned over to the District.

One of Governor Williams' goals for the year was reaching contributions of $100,000 for the Rotary Foundation. The goal was not achieved but he came close. The final total was $77,639 and represented the second highest figure of contributions to the Foundation’s general program fund to date. Arch Klumph Awards accounted for about 1/3 of the total and the three major gifts cited earlier certainly helped. The Foundation’s Share Program would credit over $46,500 to the District for program use in the 1996-97 Rotary year.

President Barth held his International Convention in Taipei, Taiwan, China June 10 - 15, 1994. Among those attending the convention from the District were DGN Chuck LaBarr and Faye and PDRI Ralph McLaughlin and Billye.

Governor Williams and Rita made the trek to Pampa on June 30th, 1994 to pass the District Governor’s pin to Chuck LaBarr. His thoughts on the trip ranged from, “I hope and pray that the causes of Rotary in District 5730 were not set back due to my actions, or lack of actions,” to “Rita, my love, we had a good year.” Most Rotarians would focus on the later and records conclusively indicate that they did.

The next day Donivan R. Williams joined the ranks of the PDGs. At the District Conference Rita Williams was overheard asking Moggie Breaud what she missed most about not being the wife of the District Governor. Moggie’s reply was, “We don’t get to go to the head of the line anymore.” P.D.G. : Prestige Done Gone.

1994 - 1995

This Rotary year, which began July 1, 1994, was remembered as the year that world leaders of all sorts tried to settle differences with conferences, visits, agreements, pacts, and treaties. Many of them were steps in the right direction but failed to realize the lofty goals established. China’s Prime Minister spent 10 days touring Europe in July exuding goodwill and smiles. Near the end of the month, Jordan’s King Hussein and Israel’s Prime Minister Rabin signed the Washington Declaration at the White House, ending the state of war between the two countries. A panel of U.S. federal judges named Kenneth W. Starr to replace Robert B. Fiske as the independent prosecutor in the Whitewater case. In August representatives of Taiwan and China signed an agreement of cooperation, and the outlawed Provisional Irish Republican Army declared a cease-fire in its campaign to end British rule in the province of Northern Ireland. A collective bargaining agreement failed to materialize between major league baseball players and team owners and the players went out on strike. Five weeks later the owners canceled the 1994 season including the World Series. China’s President and Russian President Yeltsin signed a series of economic and cooperation pacts in September. The same month the Haitian military-led government agreed to step down and restore the presidency of Jean-Bertrand Aristide after the U.S. threatened invasion. In October, 1994 U.S. Secretary of State Warren Christopher and China’s Foreign Minister agreed that the U.S. could export high-tech satellites to China and in return, China agreed to stop exporting surface to air missiles to the world’s troubled spots. The U.S. and North Korea signed agreements that were supposed to end the crisis over North Korea’s refusal to allow international inspections of its nuclear development sites. Three of the world’s premier peace makers were named co-winners of the 1994 Nobel Peace Prize: Israel’s Yitzhak Rabin and Shimon Peres and Palestine Liberation Organization’s Yasir Arafat.

In November, 1994 in South Carolina, Susan V. Smith was arrested and charged with murdering her two small children after claiming they were abducted in a carjacking. The November elections resulted in a major sweep for Republicans who won both houses of Congress and captured several major gubernatorial races, including Texas. A short time later U.S. Representative Newt Gingrich (R-GA) was selected as speaker of the 104th Congress. Secretary of the Treasury Lloyd M. Bentsen, Jr. resigned from his post and controversial U.S. Surgeon General Joycelyn Elders was forced out of her office. Near the end of the year 34 Western Hemisphere nations concluded a Summit of the Americas by agreeing to create a comprehensive free-trade zone by the year 2005. President Clinton gave his State of the Union address on Jan. 24, 1995 and called for a smaller, more efficient federal government. Less than two weeks later he proposed a $1.610 trillion budget for the fiscal year 1996. The U.S. and Vietnam agreed to exchange diplomats, the U.S. loaned Mexico $20 billion to help it avoid defaulting on short term debts, Speaker of the House Newt Gingrich began work on the “Contract with America,” and opening arguments were presented in the murder trial of O.J. Simpson who was accused of killing his former wife, Nicole Brown Simpson and her friend Ronald Goldman.

In March, 1995 basketball star Michael Jordan rejoined the Chicago Bulls after retiring in 1993. A nerve-gas attack by terrorists paralyzed the subway system of Tokyo killing 10 persons. A month later on April 19, 1995 a massive car bomb exploded outside a federal office building in Oklahoma City causing numerous fatalities and extensive damage.

Yachting fans in America mourned the loss of America’s Cup to New Zealand in May, 1995. The Kiwis exulted in their innovation of the “winged keel” as the deciding factor in the races. Many Americans were also disheartened when the U.S. Supreme Court ruled that states could not enact term limits for members of Congress, effectively overruling legislation passed by 23 states. On the last day of this Rotary year, June 30, 1995, a U.S. space shuttle docked with a Russian space station for the first time.

The world of Rotary continued to set lofty goals and kept right on track in achieving them. To lead the world’s premier service organization, one of Rotary’s most gifted speakers, Bill Huntley of Alford and Mablethorpe, England was installed as President of Rotary International on July 1, 1994. President Huntley’s theme for the year was “Be a Friend,” and it was a theme that he took quite seriously. During his year Rotary President Huntley, along with the World Health Organization, UNICEF, and others, celebrated eradication of polio in the Americas. The Council on Legislation, meeting in Venezuela, adopted a resolution affirming global polio eradication as “a priority of the highest order for all of R.I.” President Huntley held six Friendship Conferences in different parts of the world to highlight Rotary service projects aimed at community improvement. In celebration of Rotary’s 90th anniversary Rotary World Window Week was held 19-25 February, 1995 featuring public displays about Rotary service projects by clubs around the globe. Rotary World newspaper was launched, replacing several Rotary publications. Approximately 1200 Foundation Scholarships were awarded. Rotarians gathered in Nice, France for the International Convention, and gather they did. More than 34,000 Rotarians and guests registered and were housed in hotels from the Italian border to Marseilles.

In late June, 1994 Governor Don Williams and Rita drove to Pampa to officially pin the new governor, Charles “Chuck” LaBarr, and to recognize his wife, Faye, as the ‘first lady’ of District 5730. On July lst it became official and the district began its new year with continued leadership of the highest order. Commitment to Rotary, organization, involvement, motivation, and leadership by example were Governor LaBarr’s strong suits and he plied them well.

Governor LaBarr was born and reared in Peoria, Illinois. His first career was in the military where he spent over 20 years in the United State Air Force, retiring as a Lt. Col. His second career was devoted to consulting in the field of government contracts and the Aerospace Industry. His third career was Rotary. He married Faye in Westchester, California in 1974, they have a son, and he presented them with two grand daughters.

Governor LaBarr’s involvement in Rotary began in June, 1978 when he was inducted as a member of the Westchester Rotary Club in Westchester, California, District 5280. He served that club in many capacities and became club president in 1986-87. In 1988 he moved to Pampa, Texas and was immediately involved in that Rotary Club. He served a second club presidency in Pampa in 1991-92. His abilities did not go unnoticed in the district. He was selected by Governor Jim Cook to be his Special Representative in 1991-92 and repeated that task for Governor Cliff Breaud in 1992-93. The “President of the Year” award was presented to him at the District Conference in 1992. Governor LaBarr and Faye were both 5 level Paul Harris Fellows and Benefactors of the Rotary Foundation. Their son, Ed, is also a Paul Harris Fellow.

Other civic activities for the governor included the presidency of the Phoenix, AZ. Thunderbird Chapter of the National Contract Management Association and the Department of Defense Ten Year Club in Los Angeles, CA. He served as president of the Pampa Shrine Club in 1993 and was an active member of the Top ‘O Texas Knife and Fork Club, the Air Force Association, and the Retired Offices Association.

Governor LaBarr and Faye did not sit still during his year as District Governor Nominee. In the Spring, 1993 they attended the Lubbock District Conference, the Plainview District Assembly, and the three day PETS meeting in Dallas. Girls’ RYLA was on the agenda that summer. The six day Zone 5-11 Institute in Lafayette, LA. and the Rotary Foundation Seminar were attended during the Fall, 1993, then they were off to the eight day training session of the R.I. Assembly in Anaheim, CA. in March, 1994. This experience was immediately followed by the District Conference in Odessa, PETS in Dallas, and his District Assembly in Levelland. Governor LaBarr and Faye then attended the Rotary International Convention in Taipei, Tiawan before coming home for the pinning ceremony. Other Rotarians seen at the convention included George and Iris Keeling (Levelland,) Kelly and Mary Hand (Lubbock,) Art and Sharon Rousseau (Southwest Lubbock,) J.B. and Ramona Roberts (Plainview,) Dan and Bama Coward (Pampa,) Joe and Margaret Lowery (Pampa,) and DRI Ralph and Billye McLaughlin (Big Spring.)

Thoroughly saturated with Rotary information Governor LaBarr and Faye began their official visits to the 54 clubs in the district on July 5, 1994. They met the following club presidents and secretaries:

The Governor wasn’t the only one active in the District’s business. On June 26-July 1, 1994 John Heetland’s team held Boys’ RYLA at Camp Summer Life near Taos. It was followed on July 25 - 30 by Girls’ RYLA conducted by Cheri Sparks and her group at the same location. Dozens of Rotarian volunteers spent a week of their time with the 150+ young men and women who attended these camps. Both students and staff agreed that the camps made a terrific impact on lives.

Another great project of the district was the Diabetic Camp held at Ceta Glen near Canyon. Each summer medical personnel from the Texas Tech School of Health Sciences, Department Pediatrics, and other health serving agencies spent a week with 50+ children with diabetes in a learning experience.

The District bid farewell to the Memphis Rotary Club on July 13, 1994 when its charter was surrendered to Rotary International. Childress was the sponsoring club when the Memphis charter was issued November 14, 1924, more than seventy year earlier.

The District’s ribbon cutting ceremony for the Apple Orchard project was held on August 27, 1994 in Lubbock. There were more than 200 people in attendance to hear former Texas Governor Preston Smith give the dedication speech. Like the little apple trees, this project was destined to grow into one of the premier projects of Rotary.

While the governor and Faye were making their rounds the British invaded the District. PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) had arranged a Friendship Exchange with District 1070. Seventeen Brits led by Tom Glover visited Big Spring, Plainview, and Amarillo between September 6 - 20, 1994. It was a great experience and a very nice beginning for the district’s newest project.

Ted Holder, chair of the World Community Service Committee reported that a trip was made to Madera, Mexico September 8 - 11, 19, 1994. John Best, Lannie Lee, and Brady Hickman (Snyder,) Joe Don Hancock (Midland,) Howard Mercer (Lubbock,) and Ted Holder (Levelland) took school supplies to 400 school children in two different schools. Ted Holder reported that the people they encountered were a pleasure to be with and that District 5730 was making a difference in the lives of hundreds of families.

PDGs, DGN Doyle Moore, and Governor LaBarr assembled in Overland Park, Kansas for the Zone 5 - 11 Institute that was held September 29 - October 4, 1994. They were accompanied by their spouses and enjoyed a 6 day orientation and training on the latest in Rotary programs and information. Incoming governor Doyle Moore was greeted by eleven of his colleagues from District 5730 during his ‘presentation’ at that meeting.

Rotarians gathered in Lubbock on November 5, 1994 for the Rotary Foundation Seminar organized by PDG Ed Self (Plainview.) Every aspect of the Foundation was covered by an array of speakers drawn from the district. The meeting was held at the Lubbock Country Club and featured Past President of R.I. Clifford Dochterman as the evening speaker.

The Group Study Exchange team to India was assembled during the 1994-95 year by Dr. Jeff Stuyt, District GSE chair, and his committee. The team leader was Dr. Mike Graves (Plainview.) He was accompanied by Margaret A. Jenkins (Amarillo,) Don “Mike” Adams (Big Spring,) Sandra F. Lamb (Midland,) and Dolly A . Ramirez (Colorado City.) The team departed for District 3090 in India on January 28, 1995 and returned February 25th.

The Trustees of the Rotary Foundation approved two matching grants, one for sewing machines for a small community in District 3090 and computer equipment for a public school in Sunham, India. These were the second and third such grants in our District.

During his official visits to the 54 clubs in the district and throughout his year Governor LaBarr stressed the goals that he had established. Specifically addressed were the Four Avenues of Service and the Rotary Foundation. The governor wisely choose a group of knowledgeable Rotarians to assist him with these tasks and they included the following: Fred Brook (Pampa) - District Secretary; Doug Ware (Pampa) - Treasurer; PDG Don Williams (Odessa) - Nominations; Ron Bailey (Lubbock) - Free Enterprise; Tommy Patterson (S.W. Lubbock) - Diabetic Camp; Don Cain (Pampa) - Resolutions; Margaret Lutherer (Lubbock) - Public Relations; PDG J. D. Cage (Muleshoe) - Rotary Extension; W. L. Goble (Levelland) - District Liability Insurance; John Heetland (Amarillo West) - Boys’ RYLA; Dr. Cheri T. Sparks (Big Spring) - Girls’ RYLA; PDG Ed Self (Plainview) - Rotary Foundation; Jeff Stuyt (Lubbock) - Group Study Exchange; Kenneth L. Ketner (Lubbock) - Scholarships; PRID Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) - PolioPlus; PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West) - Matching Grants; PDG Bob Lewis (Big Spring) - Planned Giving; Dudley Faver (Lubbock) - Rotary Information; PDG Bill Hubbs (Pecos) - Club Service; PDG J. Davis Armistead (Lubbock) - Membership Development; PDG Jack Selby (Lubbock) - Attendance; Joe Lowry (Pampa) - Club Awards; Bruce Roberson (Perryton) - Co-Chair; Michael Tandy (Midland) - Vocational Service; PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock) - Community Service; Robert Taylor (Lubbock) - Interact and Rotaract; Ted Holder (Levelland) - International Service and World Community Service; PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) - Friendship Exchange; Lee George (Big Spring) - Youth Exchange; and Mike Graves (Plainview) - Recreational and Vocational Fellowships.

Governor LaBarr selected a dynamic team of Special Representatives to assist him with District business and club relations. They included Curt Beck (Pampa,) Doug Kile (Perryton,) Paul Garcia (Dimmitt,) David Debusk (Plainview,) Marvin Baker (Levelland,) Eldon Davidson (Amarillo East,) David Cobb (Lubbock,) Travis LaGrone (Lamesa,) Curtis Saylor (Odessa,) Tim Fambrough (Sweetwater,) Dan Gibbs (Monahans,) and James Satterwhite (Seminole.)

Lee George (Big Spring) reported a busy year for Youth Exchange in the District. Twice during the year Governor LaBarr and Faye hosted the visiting exchangers in their home. On the first visit the students prepared their favorite foods from their country. Faye reported that she had a very busy kitchen on that occasion.

Governor LaBarr was notified in January, 1995 that District 5730 had been awarded a Group Study Exchange with District 4790 in Argentina. The exchange was to take place during the 1995-96 Rotary year.

Dr. Ken Ketner, District chair of the Ambassadorial Scholarship program announced that his committee had selected two students from Texas Tech to receive scholarships for the 1996-97 academic year: Nyamusi K. Igami who planned to study in Mexico, and Paul Byrne, II who indicated a preference for study in Germany. The value of each scholarship was approximately $21,500.

PRID Ralph McLaughlin was District 5730’s representative at the Rotary International Council on Legislation that met in Caracas, Venezuela in early 1995. This was Ralph’s fifth Council. At his own expense he attended four others as the District’s Alternate Representative that met in San Francisco, Chicago, Chicago, and Singapore. Rotary’s Council on Legislation was a grueling affair that was held every third year. Each council took several days to complete, started early, ended late, and required a great deal of preparation and study.

On February 23, 1995 the Rotary International Assembly began in Anaheim, California. Incoming Governor Doyle Moore and Doris attended and got the full dose of what Rotary was all about. The Assembly was an intensive seminar on all aspects of Rotary that spanned eight days.

The highlight of the year occurred in Pampa on March 9 - 14, 1995 at the Coronado Inn. Governor LaBarr and his committee of Pampa Rotarians staged an outstanding conference that was filled with fun, fellowship, and Rotary. Those responsible for the affair included Rex McAnelly and Charlene Morriss - Conference Chairs; Ginger McVay - Conference Secretary; Lee Waters - Resolutions/Credentials; Charles Powell - Sgt.-At-Arms; Larry Price - Door Prizes and Promotion/Publicity; Charlie White - House; Bruce Roberson - Ceremonies; Roberta’s Flowers - Courtesy Flowers; Bob Neslage - Golf; Charles Fleming - Transportation; Curt Beck Exhibits/Displays; Nanette Moore and Paulette Kirksey - Decorations/Activities; Charles Powell - Store Manager; and Myrna Orr- Music.

R.I. President Huntley assigned one of the premier rising stars of Rotary to be his Special Representative to Governor LaBarr’s conference. PDG Mike McCullough and Sherry came to Pampa with their enthusiasm for Rotary at a high level. They were from District 6400 and Trenton, Michigan. Mike possessed all of the personal, civic, and Rotary credentials that a special representative should have and was remembered for his ‘round tuits.’

Preliminary conference business included a District Governor’s Advisory Conference meeting and a PDG’s dinner meeting. The plenary sessions that followed the next morning included Governor LaBarr’s state of the district address and a report by Special Representative Mike McCullough. Mike was the featured speaker at the noon luncheon. The afternoon was filled with presentations about the Council on Legislation by PRID Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring,) friendship exchange by PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring,) membership development by PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo,) and mentoring by G. B Thompson (Amarillo South.) Friday evening was filled with a shrimp feast at the M.K. Brown Center with entertainment by the Pampa High School Choir.

Saturday morning’s plenary sessions were devoted to presentations on the apple orchard by PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock,) Group Study Exchange by Jeff Stuyt (Lubbock) and Mike Graves (Plainview,) Boys’ RYLA by John Heetland (S.W. Amarillo,) World Community Service Projects by Ted Holder (Levelland,) and PolioPlus by PRID Ralph McLaughlin. PDG Ed Self (Plainview) and PDG Bob Lewis (Big Spring) discussed the Foundation and Ken Ketner (Lubbock) presented information on the Ambassadorial Scholarship program.

The motivational lunch held at noon on Saturday featured Dr. Max Brown (Amarillo) as the speaker. Dr. Brown was the Vice President for Development at the High Plains Baptist Hospital in Amarillo. After his speech ‘Rotary Club of the Year’ awards were presented to Plainview (large clubs,) Borger (medium clubs,) and Spearman (small clubs.) Fred Neslage (Pampa) was recognized for his 50 years of perfect attendance. ‘Outstanding Bulletin’ awards were given to Midland’s Rotary Table, Tahoka’s Stemwinder, and Amarillo West’s Gears.

That afternoon Mike Tandy (Midland) presented information on Vocational Service, Lee George (Big Spring) described Youth Exchange activities, and Judge Lee Waters (Pampa) presented the conference resolutions citing efforts of Presidents Representative Mike and Sherry McCullough, Governor Chuck and Faye LaBarr, and Conference Chair Rex McAnelly and the Pampa Rotary Club.

Saturday evening the Governor’s Banquet featured a stirring speech by R.I. President’s Representative Mike McCullough, presentation of The Rotary Foundation’s ‘Citation for Meritorious Service’ to a very surprised PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West,) and a presentation of the Foundation’s crystal to PDG Don Williams for his major gift to the Foundation. Don also received Rotary International’s ‘Service Above Self’ award. Kathlene Thornton, wife of Lockney Rotarian Owen Thornton, designed and tailored a jacket made from club banners collected by Governor LaBarr that was auctioned with proceeds going to the Foundation. J. B. Roberts (Plainview) was the high bidder and paid $1200 for it. Several Paul Harris awards were made and 9 new Benefactors recognized. J. B. Roberts (Plainview) was selected as ‘The Rotarian of the Year.’ A dance was held with music provided by the Canyon Rotary Band, directed by Dudley Moore and Raymond Raillard.

Sunday morning Dr. Ed Cooley (Pampa) directed a non denominational service, Curt Beck presented the District’s necrology observance, a brunch was served, Auld Lang Syne was sung and the 1995 Rotary District Conference was history.

Total registration for the event was 174 Rotarians and guests and they represented 30 of the District’s 54 clubs. Governor LaBarr was quite satisfied with the efforts put forth by all of those involved in the conference.

The Rotary year was by no means ended at this point. PDG Don Williams (Odessa) reported that a lawyer from Snyder, Marvin Sentell, had been nominated by his committee to serve as District Governor in 1996-97.

Governor LaBarr reported that the PETS meeting in Dallas, March 23-26, 1995 was attended by 40 of the District’s 54 club presidents elect. Governor LaBarr was joined by DGN Doyle Moore (Amarillo,) DGNN Marvin Sentell (Snyder,) four PDG’s, and all of their spouses.

April, 1995 was joyous for three Rotary Clubs for they were cited by Rotary International with ‘Presidential Citations.’ Achieving this rigorous goal were the clubs of Metropolitan Lubbock, Plainview, and Greater Odessa.

The Group Study Exchange team from District 3090 in India arrived in Lubbock on April 30, 1995 where they were met by GSE chair Jeff Stuyt and their Lubbock host families. The team was led by Rotarian Achhr Kumar Bansal (Samana) who was accompanied by Parshotam Kumar Singla (Bathinda,) Seema Goyal (Mudki,) Rohit Singla (Patiala,) and Anish Singla (Patran.) The team made stops in Big Spring, Colorado City, Levelland, Pampa, Plainview and Amarillo during their month long tour. They departed for Dallas on May 27th, 1995.

One of the two major District meetings held each year was the District Assembly, a meeting designed to motivate, inspire, and provide Rotary knowledge and instruction to incoming club officers. May 13, 1995 at the Plainview Country Club was the time and place of the 1994-95 Assembly. DGN Doyle Moore convened the meeting and was joined by many other Rotarians from across the district to outline the programs of Rotary for the coming year. Membership growth and development received special emphasis. Twenty-nine clubs represented by 143 members were registered for the conference.

PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) reported that 20 Rotarians and spouses participated in the District Friendship Exchange return visit to District 1070 in England. The group departed the latter part of May, 1995 for their 15 day adventure and included
DGN Doyle and Doris Moore (Amarillo,) PDG Paige and Norma Carruth (Amarillo,) Barbara Miller (Amarillo,) Beth Duke (Amarillo West,) G. B. and Gertrude Thompson (Amarillo South and Amarillo East,) PDG Ed and Maryana Self (Plainview,) Jack and Murna Miller (Plainview,) PRID Ralph and Billye McLaughlin (Big Spring,) PDG Charles and Joan Beil (Big Spring,) Hayes & Dorothy Stripling (Big Spring,) and Jerry & Louise Worthy (Plainview.)

The Rotary International Convention was held in Nice, France June 11 - 14 and District 5730 was well represented. Dudley Favor (Lubbock) was coordinator for an exhibit featuring the District’s Apple Orchard project that attracted a great deal of attention. Doris Moore (Amarillo) took Governor LaBarr’s club banner jacket to the convention and really stood out in the crowd while wearing it. DGN Doyle Moore and PRID Ralph McLaughlin and their spouses got the good hotel rooms in Nice. The rest of those in attendance were scattered all over the South of France.

A Rotarian who had a long and distinguished career, PDG Morris Higley of Childress, died June 29, 1995. PDG Higley was publisher of the Childress Herald and kept his surrounding communities aware of what Rotary was doing for six decades. Morris was two months shy of having 60 years of perfect attendance in Rotary at the time of his death.

The final numbers attest to the fact that Governor LaBarr had a good year as Governor of District 5730. Contributions to the Rotary Foundation totaled $57,777.92 during the year, 60% of which was credited to the District three years later for Foundation programs in accordance with the Share Program. Governor LaBarr welcomed 40 new Paul Harris Fellows, 24 new Benefactors of the Rotary Foundation, and an estimated 15 new sustaining members of the Foundation. Membership in the 54 clubs in the District totaled 2528 members at the beginning of his year and ended with 2558 members, a net gain of 30 members. Additional good news concerned the finances of the district. Governor LaBarr’s end of the year report showed a balance of $96,252.36, about half of which was restricted funds belonging to the RYLA Camps, Youth Exchange, and Matching Grants programs.

In summing up his year Governor LaBarr said, “District 5730 has the most unique clubs in that all of them are proud of their cities and show great community spirit and pride. The diversity of the products grown and manufactured, the farm lands, rolling plains and oil fields lend credibility to its people who work with dedication and service to their communities.”

1995 - 1996

News events followed by Rotarians in this era after the cold war indicated that people in the world were still having trouble getting along. This Rotary year got underway in July, 1995 with peace initiatives in several of the world’s troubled spots, terrorist initiatives designed to derail those peace overtures, and politics as usual in most places. In July the U.S. Senate began hearings into the Whitewater affair and a Palestinian Islamist detonated a bomb on a public bus in Tel Aviv, thought to be in protest of talks between the Israelis and PLO leader Yasir Arafat. Terrorist also set off a bomb in a crowded subway in Paris killing seven and injuring scores, an event significant to three Amarillo Rotarian couples in District 5730 who were on that train four weeks earlier. In August Americans chuckled when two of Saddam Hussein’s sons-in-law defected to Jordan, were saddened to learn of the death of Yankee’s great Mickey Mantle, and concerned about their local banks when the new ‘largest bank’ in the U.S. was formed with the merger of Chemical Banking Corp. and Chase Manhattan Corp.

In September Lou Gehrig’s 1939 record of 2,130 consecutive games played was passed to Cal Ripken, Jr. of the Baltimore Orioles. Senator Bob Packwood (R-OR) resigned amid charges of sexual misconduct. Israel’s Prime Minister Rabin and PLO Chairman Arafat signed more agreements on Palestinian autonomy, angering groups on both sides of those issues. In October a court in New York convicted 10 Muslims for blowing up the World Trade Center in New York in 1993 while another jury in California found O.J. Simpson not guilty of killing his former wife and her friend. Louis Farrakhan’s ‘Million Man March’ attracted thousands and was held in Washington D.C. World leaders, including several prominent Rotarians, gathered at the United Nations to mark its 50th anniversary. Israel’s Prime Minister Yitzhak Rabin was assassinated by a fellow countryman, retired U.S. General Colin Powell announced that he would not seek the U.S presidency in 1996, and in Poland Lech Walesa’s era came to an end. A partial shutdown of the federal government occurred briefly in November when President Clinton vetoed a stopgap measure to fund the government. The presidents of Bosnia, Serbia and Croatia signed still another peace agreement at Wright-Patterson Air Force Base in Ohio on Nov. 21st calling for 60,000 NATO troops (20,000 Americans) to enforce it. A union that began with great fanfare neared an end when Britain’s Queen Elizabeth threw in the towel and urged Prince Charles to divorce Princess Diana.

In January, 1996 President Clinton delivered his State of the Union message, declaring that the “era of big government has ended.” The hopes of the Pittsburgh Steelers for a Super Bowl victory ended also when they were defeated 27 - 17 by the Dallas Cowboys in Super Bowl XXX.

Leaders from Bosnia, Serbia, and Croatia agreed to stop fighting once again, huge suicide bombs were the rage in the Near East, Alan Greenspan got another term as chair of the Federal Reserve Board, comedian George Burns died 7 weeks after his 100th birthday, and the Menendez brothers, who confessed, were finally found guilty of murdering their parents in Beverly Hills, California. In April, 1996 a man accused of being the “Unabomber” was arrested after an 18 years search, and Dan Rostenkowski, former chair of the U.S. House Ways and Mean Committee, went to jail for mail fraud. Terrorists in the Middle East were temporarily successful in disrupting the peace process between Israel and the P.L.O. but world leaders got it back on an unsteady track. Bob Dole (R-Kan) resigned from the Senate to run for the presidency, and three people from Arkansas were convicted in a “Whitewater” trial: James and Susan McDougal and Governor Jim Guy Tucker. About 400 improperly obtained confidential FBI files were discovered in the White House, the “Freemen” ended an 81 day standoff with authorities in Jordan, Montana, and the Supreme Court admitted women to state supported Virginia Military Institute.

Conditions for peace and harmony were much better in the world of Rotary. On July 1, 1995 Rotarian Herbert C. Brown of Clearwater, Florida became the President of Rotary International. His theme for the year urged Rotarians to “Act with Integrity, Serve with Love, Work for Peace.” Geoffrey Large was installed as R.I. General Secretary, the Rotary world was reorganized into 34 Zones, and membership was opened to qualified retired persons. The time permitted for making up a missed Rotary meeting was extended to 14 days. Contributions to the Rotary Foundation Annual Programs Fund totaled $56.3 million, the Permanent Fund received $7.2 million boosting its market value to $46.8 million, and total PolioPlus contributions including earned income since the program began in 1988 raised revenues to a whopping $382 million. Ambassadorial Scholarships awarded during this year totaled 1,215 and resulted in expenditures of $20.6 million.

District 5730 continued to benefit from top quality leadership in 1995 - 1996. The District was accustomed to Rotarians who provided planning, organization, supervision, and control and that is exactly what they got when Doyle Moore, member of The Rotary Club of Amarillo, was pinned as governor on July 1, 1995 by PDG Chuck LaBarr of Pampa. Governor Moore’s lovely wife, Doris, who became known as ‘The Governess’ throughout the District, was also a member of The Rotary Club of Amarillo. Like all of the first ladies before her, she added charm, wit, beauty, and class to the Governor’s act. Two Rotarians for the price of one was the standard set during this Rotary year.

Governor Moore was a native of Amarillo and a graduate of Amarillo High School. He earned BBA and MBA degrees from West Texas State University, served a four year enlistment in the U.S. Navy during the Korean conflict, then joined Southwestern Public Service Company where he worked for almost 40 years. Upon his retirement in January, 1995 Governor Moore was a division manager and a member of the Management Committee.

Governor Moore married Doris Wrather of Amarillo. They raised one daughter, Diane, who presented them with three grandchildren. The Moores were multiple Paul Harris Fellows and Benefactors of the Rotary Foundation. Both were active in the civic affairs of Amarillo. Governor Moore served as president of Camp Fire, Salvation Army, and the Knife and Fork Club. He was a vice president for Boy Scouts and served as a board member of the Better Business Bureau, Amarillo College Foundation, Amarillo Chamber of Commerce, and Texas Panhandle Heritage Foundation. Doris was a member of the board of the Amarillo Chamber of Commerce, served as president of the Women’s Auxiliary of the Chamber, was a member of the Potter County Extension Advisory Board, Secretary of the Samaritan Counseling Board, and was selected by the Chamber of Commerce as “Business Woman of the Year” in 1995. The family was active in the St. Paul’s Methodist Church, its education programs, choir, and official board.

Governor Moore joined The Rotary Club of Amarillo in 1982 and served as president in 1989-90. He continued his involvement with District 5730 affairs after his presidency by working with the Diabetic Camp Committee and taking part in District Conferences. PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock) chaired the nominations committee in 1993, conducted interviews with both of the Moores, and announced the selection of Doyle Moore as their choice for District Governor for the year 1995 - 1996. His official training for the job began with the Zone 5-11 Institute in Overland Park, Kansas, a meeting of incoming, current, and past officers of Rotary International. Training, motivation, and fellowship spanned six days beginning on Sept. 27 and ending Oct. 2, 1994. Eleven PDGs and spouses from District 573 witnessed the Moore’s presentation. In Feb., 1995 DGN Moore and Doris traveled to Anaheim, California for the 10 day Rotary Institute where they were joined by their 500+ counterparts from all over the Rotary World for an intensive and in-depth orientation concerning the many facets of Rotary. The month of March, 1995 was equally busy for they participated in the three day District Conference in Pampa and the three day President-Elect Training Seminar (PETS) held in Dallas. DGN Moore participated in the interviews conducted with applicants for the Ambassadorial Scholarship awards on May 6th in Lubbock and joined Governor LaBarr for the District Assembly that was held in Plainview May 13, 1995. In June they participated in a two week Friendship Exchange in England, attended the Rotary International Convention in Nice, France and upon arriving home made visits to Girls’ RYLA, Boys’ RYLA, and the Diabetic Camp. Regarding his year of training, Governor Moore was heard to say, “I now feel ready to serve as president of my Rotary Club.”

Governor Moore started his official visits to the 54 clubs in the District on July 19, 1995. He felt this was a late start but wanted time to visit the RYLA camps and give club presidents time to get settled in their jobs. He might have wanted to catch his breath as well. After driving more than 9,000 miles and staying out 45 nights the club assemblies were completed with a triumphant visit to The Rotary Club of Amarillo on Nov. 30, 1995. Club presidents and secretaries that he worked with during the year included the following Rotarians:
