During his visits with clubs Governor Moore stressed the action word “Grow.” He urged all clubs to grow in membership, knowledge, commitment, service, fellowship, involvement, and Rotary Foundation support. Following RI President Herb Brown’s lead Governor Moore placed a great deal of emphasis on membership growth in an effort to reverse the trend of declining membership in existing clubs. PDG Mike Penson (Kileen) called for all Zone 5 Governors and Membership Chairmen to meet with him in Kileen on July 22, 1995 where a detailed procedure was put into place to address this problem. Governor Moore, PDG Ralph McLaughlin, and PDG Paige Carruth attended this meeting. Each Governor of the Zone was urged to hold a Membership Development Seminar in their District. With the help of his Area Representatives Governor Moore proceeded to hold three seminars in District 5730 in August and September, 1995. Ninety-two Rotarians attended these meetings in Lubbock, Odessa, and Amarillo. PDRI Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring,) R.I. National Coordinator for the Membership Development Task Force, made presentations at each seminar, handed out membership proposal cards, and insisted that members use them. PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo) described the District’s ASPIRE (A Special Program In Rotary Education) program he designed to retain club members, and Governor Moore outlined the magnitude and seriousness of local attention to membership development. After the seminars were held Governor Moore distributed District-wide more than 100 approaches helpful in recruiting and retaining club members. The focus of this activity was directed toward leadership on the club level. Monthly membership reports were collected by Ben Conner (Borger,) J. David Mims (Midland,) and J.B. Roberts (Plainview,) and were transmitted through channels to R.I. during the year. The efforts paid off in District 5730 for at the end of the year club presidents reported an increase of 55 members in their clubs, short of the Governor’s goal of a 5% expansion, but an increase nevertheless.

Believing that all clubs would benefit from knowing of the projects being done in the District, Governor Moore compiled a massive list of activities including fund raisers being carried out by Rotarians gleaned from the ‘Club Plans and Objectives’ reports. It was 11 pages long, single spaced, a testimony to the involvement of club members in Service Above Self, and the Governor’s willingness to put a lot of work into sharing ideas. This was a treasure of ideas and a valuable resource for clubs to use in years to come.

In his District Directory the Governor included very specific and measurable goals, a piece of research that contained all of the 54 club’s charter dates, sponsoring clubs and their progeny, plus the rich resources of Rotarians available to clubs in developing the Four Avenues of Service locally. District Committee Chairs included the following:

Dale Bippus (Amarillo) - Secretary; Marilyn Ault, CPA (Amarillo) - Treasurer; Fred Chesser (Amarillo South) - District Conference; Joe D. Parrott (Amarillo West) - District Conference Comptroller; PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa) - Nominations; W. L. Goble (Lubbock) - Liability Insurance; Jon Oden (Amarillo) - Resolutions; Margaret Lutherer (Lubbock) - Public Relations; and PDG Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) - PolioPlus.

PDG Bill Hubbs (Pecos) chaired the Club Service Committee. Assisting him were PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo,) Ben Conner (Borger,) J. David Mims (Midland,) and J.B. Roberts (Plainview) - Membership Development; and Kathy Cornett (Amarillo) - Club Bulletins and Awards. George Keeling (Levelland) chaired Community Service, and Wynon Mayes (Canyon) headed Vocational Service.

PDG Ed Self (Plainview) coordinated the Rotary Foundation area and was assisted by PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock) - Benefactors and Bequests, PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West) - Matching Grants, Dr. Kenneth Ketner (Lubbock) - Ambassadorial Scholarships, Lynn Simpson (Big Spring) - Group Study Exchange, and Beth Duke (Amarillo West) - Foundation Alumni Coordinator.

Nine Rotarians worked in the Youth Service area: Lee George (Big Spring) Youth Exchange; Bob Strange (Lubbock) - Inbound Students; Randy Brilhart (Perryton) - Outbound Students; Jennifer Shirey (Metro Lubbock) - Youth Exchange Activities Director; Mike Tandy (Odessa) - Summer Cultural Exchanges; Kerry Gilmore (Lubbock) - Youth Exchange Insurance; John Heetland (Amarillo West) - Boys’ RYLA; Linda Conway (Big Spring) - Girls’ RYLA; and Barry Orr (Lubbock Southwest) - the Diabetic Camp.

Howard Wilkerson (Canyon) chaired Recreational and Vocational Fellowship Groups, Ted Holder (Levelland) coordinated International Service and World Community Service activities, and PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) continued with Friendship Exchange.

Governor Moore selected the following Rotarians to be his Area Representatives: Curt Beck (Pampa,) Doug Kile (Perryton,) R. M. Keeney (Dumas,) David DeBusk (Plainview,) Doris Reding (Levelland,) Henry Janhsen (Amarillo South,) David Cobb (Lubbock,) Travis LaGrone (Lamesa,) Curtis Saylor (Odessa,) Tim Fambrough (Sweetwater,) Layne Nutt (Kermit,) and David Shuler (Seminole.)

Clubs and Rotarians receiving recognition during the Fall, 1995 included Jennifer Shirey (Metro Lubbock) for her work in Youth Exchange, PDG Cliff Breaud for the Apple Orchard project, Scott and Debbie Burt (Greater Big Spring) for being named Family of the Year, Gene Shelburne (Amarillo West) for his newly published book, Canyon Club member Jack Haley for his 50+ years of perfect attendance, and David Bailey for his 25+ years of perfect attendance, Odessa for their Thanksgiving Baskets, Lubbock for their Career Day project, Jackie Finkner (Metro Lubbock) for his newsletter, Andrews for inducting 7 new members, Linda Conway (Greater Big Spring) for 6 new members and progress toward a Presidential Citation Award, and Childress for their Rotary Information section of their weekly bulletin “The Tumbleweed.”


Early in the Rotary year PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock) called for Rotarians to donate $20 to plant an apple tree in the District Apple Orchard. His current goal was to plant another 1300 apple trees. PDG Charles Beil was working on Friendship Exchanges with Districts in New Zealand and Chile and calling for participants that might be interested in those trips. Clubs were notified of a revised and simplified procedure for electing new club members and urged to put it into effect. Governor Moore put into effect a plan to increase participation in PETS by incoming club presidents. He started a fund to help pay expenses for those who could not otherwise attend the training program.

Governor Moore and Doris led the way to the Zone 5 - 11 meeting in Houston held on October 3-8, 1995. This was an important training and motivational session for incoming governors, District Governors, and PDG’s that was planned by the Zone 5 Director Sonny Brown (El Paso.) Outside of the International Assembly it was the best way District leaders could remain current on the status and programs of Rotary. Those attending included DGN Marvin and Julie Sentell (Snyder,) PDG Chuck and Faye LaBarr (Pampa,) PDRI Ralph McLaughlin and Billye (Big Spring,) PDG Bill and Pat Hubbs (Pecos,) PDG Don and Rita Williams (Odessa,) PDG Jim and Sue Cook (Amarillo West,) PDG Bob and Susan Lewis (Big Spring,) PDG Charles and Joan Beil (Big Spring,) PDG Cliff and Moggie Breaud (Lubbock,) and PDG Paige and Norma Carruth (Amarillo.) The reorganization of Rotary Zones caused this meeting to be the last for District 5730 in Zone 5 - 11. Our District was grouped in Zone 26 along with the eight other Districts in Texas, two in Oklahoma, and one in Louisiana. Zone meetings were scheduled to be held jointly with Zone 25.

PDG Charles Beil’s Friendship Exchange Committee arranged for twenty-three Rotarians and spouses from New Zealand to visit Amarillo, Big Spring, Midland, and Plainview for 15 days during October, 1995. Eighteen travelers from District 5730 visited New Zealand in March, 1996. They were led by Tom Beck (Amarillo.)

A Friendship Exchange with Chile, D4340, was one-half completed during this Rotary year. Four Rotarians visited District 5730 in April, 1996. They were led by Elena T. Sequel and were hosted in Big Spring, Lubbock, and Perryton.

The Fall of 1995 was a time of celebration for four clubs. President Bobby Bain of the Post Rotary Club presided over his club’s recognition of their 70th Anniversary on October 5, 1995. The Levelland Breakfast Club held their 10th anniversary gala on December 10 under the direction of club president Lee Ann Edwards, and the Greater Lubbock Rotary Club held a dual Christmas Party - 25th Anniversary Party on December 18th with club president Lon Miller presiding. Hereford combined their 50th Anniversary ceremonies with their annual Christmas Party where club president Dennis Hicks received a congratulatory certificate from R.I. President Herb Brown.

Amarillo South held a recognition ceremony of a different nature in December, 1995 when they recognized the efforts of Marilyn Van Petten and Dr. G. B. Thompson for developing and expanding a Mentoring Program. Eight Amarillo area high schools and Amarillo College were represented at the function. The program had grown to 69 Mentees/Mentors that year. Rotarian Van Petten was thoroughly surprised when she was presented with a Paul Harris Fellow award at the conclusion of the program.

Rotarians of the Amarillo West club bought 50 winter coats in early December that were distributed to the needy by the “Evelyn Rivers Christmas Project,” a local charity. Jim Henson, manager of J.C. Penney and John Teague, manager of Sears facilitated this project. Both were members of this club.

R.I. President Herb Brown put special emphasis on attracting qualified women into Rotary Clubs by creating an advisory panel of 12 women who met in Evanston, Ill. and was chaired by Membership Task Force Coordinator PDRI Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring.) One of the many recommendations coming from this panel was the creation of the R.I. Membership Advisory Council. Three distinguished ladies were selected to serve on this council: Beth Duke (Amarillo West,) Lilia Escajeda (Amarillo South,) and Barbara Miller (Amarillo.)

The District Nominating Committee chaired by PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa) announced in January that their recommendation for District Governor for the year 1997 - 1998 was J. B. Roberts of Plainview. PDG Charles Beil was busy making arrangements for Friendship Exchange visits with Chile, Sweden, and South Africa that would occur in 1996-98 and expressed hope that thirty Rotarian couples would avail themselves of this international activity. Lynn Simpson (Big Spring) announced that Jennifer Shirey (Metro Lubbock) was selected to lead the Group Study Exchange Team to District 1040 in England in the Fall, 1996.

The March, 1996 issue of The Rotarian featured an article written by PDRI Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) concerning club extension and membership growth. Cited in the article was PDG Charles Beil for the outstanding work he did in extending the number of Rotary Clubs in the District in recent years.

Governor Moore and Doris kept the road and airways hot during the winter and spring, 1996. In February they attended the part of the R.I. International Institute in Anaheim, California designed for current and past officers of Rotary and were joined by 365 others representing 39 countries. DGN Marvin Sentell and Julie were involved in the incoming officer programs of the Assembly. The Rotary Clubs of Lubbock and Plainview chose the same evening in February to pay tribute to their 75th anniversaries. Dudley Faver, president of the Lubbock Club and Michael Graves, president of the Plainview Club went to considerable lengths to insure that they did things right. Governor Moore was asked to speak at both events and accepted the invitations. He was at the first part of the Lubbock Club’s festivities and made the latter part of the Plainview affair. It is rumored that he and Doris ate a sack lunch while traveling between the two feasts. Steve Teichelman, president of the Childress Rotary Club presided over their club’s 75th anniversary in May, 1996. Guests included Governor Moore, DGN Marvin Sentell, PDG Paige Carruth, PDG Chuck LaBarr, their spouses, and representatives from many Childress organizations. Other clubs reaching significant milestones in their history during the spring included Canadian (their 70th) and Dimmitt (their 30th.)

Because of an idea by PDG Earl Wilbur (Dalhart,) The Dalhart Rotary Club made history at 3:30 PM on March 3, 1996. At that time Benjamin Allen became the youngest Paul Harris Fellow in all of Rotary at the age of 8 hours. The parents, Will and Rotarian Kim Allen were joined in the hospital room by club president Bing Seal and president-elect Butch Like who brought the club banner and stand, PDG Earl Wilbur and son Bob who took pictures, and Governor Moore and Doris who made it official. The Paul Harris certificate, pin, and medal were presented in the carefully arranged ceremony. The medal was pinned to his blanket . Benjamin slept through the whole thing. Benjamin’s nurse, Tanya Gee, turned out to be a Youth Exchange Student from Amarillo who went to Switzerland 10 years earlier.

Larry Neal, the Slaton Rotary Club’s second club president during this year, notified Governor Moore with regrets in February, 1996 that the club had voted to disband and surrender its charter to Rotary International. Many Rotarians throughout the District were saddened by this event for they remembered the great service and leadership that Slaton had provided in previous years. The Slaton Rotary Club was sponsored by the Rotary Club of Lubbock and chartered April 21, 1925. Our District’s oldest living PDG at that time, Bruce Pember, was a member of the Slaton Club.

Larry Driskill, president of Metro Lubbock, notified the District that his club was sponsoring parent training for 20 families involved in the Head Start program. Parenting skills plus activities for their children was the focus of the 6 hour program conducted by Dr. Patricia Diskill.

Lee George, chair of the Youth Exchange Committee reported that 7 students were in our District from aboard during the Rotary year, 8 students were going to Europe during the summer, 1996, and that 10 students were scheduled to depart the District during the school year 1996 - 97 to points located on four different continents.

Rotarians with computers were accessing a great deal of Rotary information on the Internet, CompuServe, Prodigy, and America On Line during this year. Rotary International developed its home page as did many Clubs and Districts throughtout the world.

The Lone Star President-Elect Training Seminar (PETS) was held in Dallas March 21-24, 1996. Incoming presidents of Rotary clubs in the nine Rotary Districts in Texas, plus one District in Oklahoma, were invited to attend. Attendance from Rotary clubs in District 5730 was not nearly as good as it should have been. Fourteen clubs were not represented in 1995 and 20 clubs were absent in 1996 at this superb training session. Governor Moore had offered to assist with expenses from District funds but no one requested assistance from that source. Governor Moore, PDG Jim Cook Amarillo West,) PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa,) and PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo) led discussion groups, DGN Marvin Sentell was introduced at the DGN’s presentation ceremony.

The District 5730 Group Study Exchange Team departed April l, 1996 for District 4790 in Argentina for a month long visit. Rotarian Lilia Escajeda, a banker and member of the Amarillo South club, was the team leader. Non-Rotarian members of the team included Jane Zuniga (nurse, Big Spring,) Richard Sanders (prison counselor, Big Spring,) Benjamin Robles (ag. engineer, Lubbock,) and Hector Madrigal (priest, Amarillo.) The Argentina district required that our team members be fluent in Spanish and that was a major requirement in the selection process. While our GSE team was in Argentina, the District 4790 team was traversing District 5730. Their schedule included a visit to the District Conference in Amarillo.

The highlight of every Rotary District’s year culminates in the celebration of Rotary at their District Conference. Governor Moore convened his Conference in Amarillo on Thursday, April 25, 1996 at the Ambassador Hotel. Fred Chesser (Amarillo East) had the job of Conference Chairman, a job that consumed many weeks of his time. Henry Janhsen (Amarillo East) assisted Fred in many respects as the Governor’s Group Representative. Other Rotarians with major responsibilities included Joe Don Parrott (Amarillo West) - Treasurer/Program; Walter Johnson (Amarillo) - Guest Services; Ron Brown (Amarillo South) - In-House Services; Wynon Mays (Canyon) and Glenda Carper (Amarillo West) - Food Services; Kathy Cornett (Amarillo) - Publicity/Awards; John Heetland and John Dawson (Amarillo West) - Globe News Insert; Patty Bryant (Canyon) and Jane Rouk (Amarillo South) - Entertainment; Bob Pearce (Amarillo East) - Sports and Games; and Howard Wilkerson (Canyon) - Sgt. at Arms. Marla Reyman (Amarillo Ex. Sec.) served as Conference Secretary. A 20 page supplement was included in the April 23, 1996 Amarillo Globe News regarding the District Conference.

Golf, a tea for PDG’s ladies, the Governor’s Advisory Council meeting, and dinners for PDGs (Amarillo Club) and club officers (Ambassador Hotel) filled Thursday afternoon and evening. At the PDG’s Dinner Governor Moore presented R.I. President Herb Brown’s Special Representative to the Conference PDG Bill Leonard and his wife Betty. They were from Ybor City, Florida, District 6950. PDG Leonard was a university professor of economics, administrator, author, consultant, Rotarian of great distinction, and a superb golfer. His group won the golf tournament. Betty Leonard hid her Ph.D. degree very well during the Conference and participated in every aspect of it. Governor Moore remarked that President Brown would have been proud of the way the Leonards represented him at the Conference. The Leonards were hosted by PDG Paige and Norma Carruth (Amarillo.)

The First Plenary Session on Friday, April 26, 1996 included the Governor’s State of the District Address, Beth Duke’s (Amarillo West) suggestions on the use of Foundation Alumni, explanations on how Rotarians could participate in the Friendship Exchange Program by PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring,) and a report on the Diabetic Camp by Barry Orr (Southwest Lubbock.) The four Amarillo Rotary Clubs met jointly at the Conference luncheon where Mila Gibson (Amarillo) brought the house down with her operatic rendition of The Four Way Test. Special Representative Bill Leonard was the featured speaker. The afternoon was devoted to fun and games and the evening was filled with an ‘Evening at the Opery’ at the Big Texan Steak Ranch.

Awards were presented at the Saturday breakfast. Kathy Cornett (Amarillo) judged 23 entries for Best Club Bulletin. The small club award went to Dumas, the bigger club award went to Greater Odessa, the big club award went to Metro Lubbock, and the biggest club award was given to Amarillo West. At the Plenary Session that morning Lynn Simpson introduced the Group Study Exchange team from Argentina and the GSE team going to District 1040 in England in the Fall, 1996. John Heetland (Amarillo West) gave a report on Boys’ RYLA and Linda Conway presented information on Girls’ RYLA. PDG Ed Self (Plainview) gave an overview of the Rotary Foundation, Margaret Lutherer (Lubbock) discussed the essentials of club public relations, Dr. Ken Ketner (Lubbock) urged participation in the Ambassadorial Scholarship competition, and Kathy Cornett (Amarillo) talked about the importance of club bulletins.

One of the highlights of the Conference was the Saturday noon luncheon. Astronaut Major Rick Husband, NASA, Houston (formerly of Amarillo) wowed the audience with tributes to those who were important in his life. The District reciprocated by making him a Paul Harris Fellow. Additionally, because his father, the late Doug Husband, was charter member and president of the Amarillo East Rotary Club, Major Husband was made an honorary member of that club. The afternoon was filled with reports on District projects: PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo) presented information on membership development, Bob Strange (Lubbock) discussed the Youth Exchange program, PDG Cliff Breaud urged participation in the Apple Orchard project, and PRID Ralph McLaughlin gave an overview of PolioPlus. Club reports on the four avenues of service were given by representatives of clubs that had achieved substantial success in the following areas: Club Service - Douglas Moore (Lubbock Southwest;) Community Service - Jerry Vestal (Snyder,) Gary Stretcher (Borger,) and Cal Huffaker (Tahoka;) Vocational Service - Kiby Clark (Amarillo South,) and Ray Keener (Seminole;) International Service - John Velky (Amarillo East,) and Marty Runnels (Plainview;) and Fund Raisers - Edward Womble (Perryton,) Johnny Ethridge (Dimmitt,) and Melvin Edes (Canyon.)

Saturday evening was devoted to the Governor’s Banquet. Gary Moore (Amarillo West) presided, his dad, Dr. Dudley Moore (Canyon) led the singing (without editorializing,) and Governor Moore presented the following awards: Snyder for most in attendance considering distance traveled; R.I.’s Citation for Meritorious Service went to PDG Don Williams (Odessa;) PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa) received the crystal from R.I. for making a major contribution to the Rotary Foundation; and Outstanding Club awards were given to Dimmitt, Levelland, Midland, and Odessa. Governor Moore instituted a new award, “The District 5730 Wheel of Fame” plaque which would contain the names of Rotarians who made significant strides in bettering District 5730 and Rotary in general. The first five names on the plaque were well known to Rotarians in the District: J. Edd McLaughlin, Past President of R.I. (Ralls;) Rex Webster, Past Rotary International Vice President and Director (Lubbock;) Ralph McLaughlin, Past Rotary International Director (Big Spring;) John Tyler, developer of RYLA and PDG (Midland;) and Tom Amason, implementer of RYLA (Amarillo West.) Fred Chesser (Amarillo East) was named Outstanding Rotarian of the Year. Special Representative Bill Leonard (Ybor City, Florida) was the featured speaker for the evening and Barbara Tucker (Houston) thrilled the audience with songs that made everyone in the audience proud to be a Rotarian and an American.

Sunday morning began with Bob Neslage (Pampa) presiding at the final session. Conference Resolutions were presented by Jon Oden (Amarillo,) and Dick Brooks (Amarillo) led a stirring Necrology Service. Closing remarks were made by Special Representative Bill Leonard and Governor Moore, the group joined hands, sang Auld Lang Syne, and the 1996 District Conference was history.

A total of 422 Rotarians and guests registered for the conference representing 35 of the 53 Rotary Clubs in the District. Cheers where heard from the Advisory Committee when the Governor announced that the Conference showed a minute profit.

The District Assembly that was convened in Snyder on May 18, 1996. Governor Moore joined DGN Marvin Sentell (Snyder) in opening the meeting. The agenda was prepared by DGN Sentell and 107 Rotarians gathered to discuss his 1996-97 plans and objectives. Incoming club officers and committee chairs were updated on the latest programs of Rotary, District 5730 projects, and opportunities to be considered by clubs for their communities. Rotarian resource persons made presentations at the following group sessions: Presidents-Elect and Governor’s Special Representatives - DGN Marvin Sentell (Snyder), Mike Tandy (Midland), and Doris Reding (Levelland); Incoming Secretaries and Treasurers - Frank Miller (Snyder); Incoming Club Service and Vocational Service Directors - PDG Don Williams (Odessa) and Jerry Vestal (Snyder); Incoming Community and International Service Directors - Joe Dominey (Midland) and Ted Holder (Levelland); Incoming Membership Directors - PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo) and Mike Graves (Plainview). PRID Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) was the speaker at the noon luncheon. The afternoon plenary session included presentations on the Benefactor Program by PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa), Annual Giving by Governor Moore, Youth Exchange by Bob Strange (Greater Lubbock), and RYLA by Claudia Heathington (O’Donnell).

The Lubbock Rotary Club shared a letter that was received from their Ambassadorial Scholar Dawn Dale who was studying music in Brussels, Belgium. Dawn reported that she had enjoyed several speaking engagements at Belgian Rotary clubs and performed at two other clubs.

On June 1, 1996 a group of Rotarians met in Lubbock to consider ways that money might be raised to fund the District’s outstanding Apple Orchard project. Representatives from each of the four Lubbock clubs plus Governor Moore, DGN Marvin Sentell (Snyder,) and DGND J. B. Roberts (Plainview) heard about plans for the first “Applebutter Festival” scheduled for Sept. 21, 1996. Cal and Susan Brints and daughter Aimee Martin planned to host the affair at their High Plains Apple Orchard east of Idaloo and offered Rotary District 5730 an opportunity become involved in the venture. Rotary was involved because Cal Brints and Aimee Martin were members of the Southwest Lubbock Rotary Club.

The Rotary International Convention was held in Calgary, Alberta Canada June 23 - 26, 1996 and District 5730 was well represented by incoming club officers, several PDGs, and members of Rotary clubs that enjoy the festive atmosphere and stimulation of one of the greatest shows on earth. Spouses, children, and guests were there in abundance. The Texas Breakfast, always a highlight, was attended by about 700 and some were not even Texans.

The final numbers for the Rotary Foundation revealed that Rotarians contributed $89,982 during the 1995-96 year, a whopping 120% of the $75,000 goal set by Governor Moore. The number of Paul Harris Fellows grew by 151, Benefactors increased by 16, and 80 new Sustaining Members were added. The Southwest Lubbock Rotary Club called on Governor Moore to present 22 new Paul Harris Fellow awards on June 3, 1996. Don Harris was the club Chairman of Foundation activities and reported with pride that the 31 club members who were not Paul Harris Fellows were all Sustaining Members. The Rotary Club of Amarillo leveraged credited money held at The Foundation as “matching funds” to encourage 51 Paul Harris Fellows. The three clubs having the highest per capita giving were Amarillo ($155.70,) Greater Odessa ($126.41,) and Childress $100.)

Twice yearly The Rotary Foundation forwarded an overall analysis of District Support to the District Governor and District Foundation Chair. Upon receiving the December 31, 1995 report, Governor Moore became curious about the current giving practices of Rotarians in the District, data that was not broken down in the report. “All Time Giving” figures were quite respectable but when individual donors who were not Rotarians were subtracted from the totals a picture of current giving emerged that was less so.

Category Historical Total Current Total

 Sustaining Members 581 277
 Paul Harris Fellows 1,359 701
Multiple Level PHFs 80 80
Benefactors 63 55

 After further treatment of these data Governor Moore concluded that 1,578 (62%) of current Rotarians had contributed little or nothing to the Foundation and that there was a continuing need to educate Rotarians about the Rotary Foundation and its important programs.

Several citations were issued by R.I. during this year. The President’s Golden Century Citation when to PDG Bob Lewis and PRID Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring,) PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa,) and PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo.) A Presidential Citation was issued to Randy Haralson (Amarillo West,) and Presidential Club Citations were presented to the Greater Big Spring, Levelland, Odessa, Greater Odessa, and Perryton Rotary Clubs.

On June 30th of every year thousands of Rotary club presidents, hundreds of district governors, several R.I. board members and one president of R.I. reflect on their past year. It is much like remembering a war in which you took part. If you were there you know what it was like. If not it would be hard to explain. ‘Mixed emotions’ was the catch phrase. Successes - many; regrets - some; omissions - several; the experience - tremendous; gratitude - indescribable; the future - aaahhhhhh! Such was the frame of mind of PDG Doyle Moore, ‘Past Governess’ Doris, and their kindred Rotarians on July 1, 1996.

1996 - 1997

 During this Rotary year Rotarians were treated to headlines in July that included news of Boris Yeltsin’s reelection, a low 5.3% U.S. unemployment figure, and a mystery of why a TWA 747 crashed in the Atlantic Ocean an hour out of New York City. In August Bob Dole and Jack Kemp were selected by Republicans to head their party’s presidential ticket while Democrats renominated Bill Clinton and Al Gore. Susan McDougal was sent to jail for refusing to answer questions posed before a federal grand jury investigating President Clinton’s involvement in the Whitewater real-estate venture. The Dow Jones industrial average exceeded the 6,000 mark in October, 1996 and the Yankees won the World Series, beating the Atlanta Braves four games to two.

In the November elections Bill Clinton became the first Democrat since FDR to win reelection, but the Republicans retained control of both houses in the U. S. Congress. In the Middle East factions on both sides continued to try to destroy peace efforts of Israeli and Palestinian negotiators. Charges of sexual harassment against commissioned and noncommissioned officers continued to pour in to U.S. Army headquarters causing top brass to wonder if their ‘hot line’ was a good idea.

The calendar year closed with the launch of U.S. space vessel Mars Pathfinder, an unmanned mission to collect data about Mars. President Clinton named Madeleine Albright as his new secretary of state and the Oakland, California school board created outrage among English teachers while delighting comedians with its decision to offer a course entitled “Ebonics.” An ethics subcommittee of the U.S. House of Representatives concluded that Speaker Newt Gingrich had used tax-exempt donations for political purposes, a violation of House rules.

The new year began with President Clinton’s inauguration and Democrats and Republicans pointing fingers at each other over campaign contributions. Ethics questions about cloning humans arose when scientists in a Scottish lab cloned a sheep. In March comedian Bill Cosby’s son was murdered in California while he was changing a tire on his car. Later that month Martin Luther King’s son expressed doubts that James Earl Ray killed his father.

Near the end of March 39 members of a cult known as Heaven’s Gate committed suicide in California. The media circulated opinions of the cult that a link existed between a UFO and the Hale-Bopp comet. During the spring there was widespread and devastating flooding in the Ohio River Valley, N. Dakota, Minnesota, and other areas of the upper Mid West.

In April the Russian space station MIR was damaged when it was struck by an unmanned supply ship resulting in substantial loss of power inside the station and concern for the safety of the crew, one who was an American astronaut. Swiss bankers became the focus of world attention in May when evidence supporting accusations of keeping “Nazi Gold” and retaining holocaust victims’ bank accounts became overwhelming. Timothy McVeigh was convicted of bombing an Oklahoma City Federal building in June and received the death penalty for his actions. Tobacco companies facing law suits by 38 states reached an agreement with them regarding reimbursement for medical costs caused by smoking. The reign of the British Empire over Hong Kong came to an end at midnight, June 30, 1997 when the government of mainland China assumed control of the colony.

At the same time the presidency of Rotary International passed from Herbert G. Brown of Clearwater, FL to Luis V. Giay of Buenos Aires, Argentina. President Giay’s theme for the year was “Build The Future With Action And Vision.” His Membership Challenge Plus continued the focus on increasing Rotary membership and retention worldwide. Through his 21 “Presidential Visits for New Generations” he called for clubs to support New Generations by working to meet their needs in the areas of health, education, human values and self-development. In March, 1997 the 50th Anniversary of Foundation’s Scholarships Program was recognized. At the end of President Giay’s year membership stood at 1,193,681 Rotarians who were members of 28,284 clubs located in 155 countries. Almost 1300 Ambassadorial Scholarships were awarded. President Giay’s International Convention was held in Glasgow, Scotland and was attended by over 23,000 Rotarians and guests.

Joining President Giay in the operation of Rotary during the 1996-97 year was the Governor of Rotary District 5730, Marvin Sentell, an attorney from Snyder, Texas where he was involved in the private practice of law. His wife, Julie, was active in the firm, serving as Marvin’s assistant and office manager. Governor Sentell was a graduate of Texas Tech University and received his LLB degree from the University of Texas School of Law in 1955. He served as an Assistant District Attorney in Fort Worth in 1958-59 and was an Assistant Attorney General in Austin from 1959-63 and again from 1966-80. He was in private practice 1963-66. His private practice in Snyder began in 1988.

Governor Sentell was active in many civic organizations in the Snyder region. At the time he became governor he was serving as a director of the Snyder Area Council on Alcohol and Drug Abuse, director and president of Historic Scurry County, Inc., and a director in the Children’s Trust Fund of Texas Family PRIDE Council. He was involved in his church and was served on its Finance Committee.

The governor married Julie Tiffany of Austin, Texas in 1975. They raised four children and were proud of their three grandchildren. Marvin’s principle hobbies were golf and reading.

District 5730 was extremely fortunate to secure the services of this knowledgeable and dedicated Rotarian during the 1996 - 1997 Rotary Year. He joined the Snyder Rotary Club in 1988, became actively involved in its projects and programs, and served as its president in 1993-94. He and Julie were ardent supporters of Rotary’s Youth Exchange Program and began serving annually as a host family in 1993. Marvin was a Paul Harris Fellow, Benefactor of the Rotary Foundation, and was a member of the International Golfing Fellowship of Rotary. Julie was also a Paul Harris Fellow. Marvin served as a member of the District Nominating Committee 1995-96.

During his year as District Governor Nominee, Marvin and Julie participated in all of the many training programs for governors, attended all District functions, and observed most of the District’s projects in action. Specifically, they attended the annual summer meeting of South Central Rotary Youth Exchange in August, 1995 in Dallas, the 5 day Zone 5-11 meeting in Houston in October, 1995, the winter meeting of the South Central Youth Exchange in Tulsa, Oklahoma in Feb., 1996, the 8 day Rotary International Assembly in Anaheim during February, 1996, 3 days of PETS in Dallas in March, the 4 day District Conference in Amarillo in April, 1996, conducted the District Assembly in Snyder on May 18, 1996, visited Camp RYLA near Ruidoso June 9-14, and attended the R.I. Convention in Calgary, Alberta, Canada in June, 1996.

After having been thoroughly immersed in the affairs of Rotary, the Sentells were highly charged and anxious to get underway. Their official visits to clubs began on July 8, 1996 and continued through November 19th. Club officers that they worked with included the following Rotarians:
