Girls’ RYLA was held July 22-27, 1996 at the Lone Tree Bible Camp near Capitan, New Mexico north of Ruidoso, New Mexico and was chaired by Linda Conway (Big Spring.) Claudia Heathington (O’Donnell) functioned as Camp Director and was assisted by about a dozen volunteers who worked as counselors and staff. This camp was very well supported by clubs in the district. Eighty-nine girls attended and participated in leadership workshops, sports activities, and rubbed shoulders with some truly inspirational speakers. Camp Director Heathington declared the project successful and was looking forward to the next year.

The South Central Rotary Youth Exchange met in Dallas August 3-4, 1996 and the Sentells represented District 5730. Inspiring talks were presented and information was exchanged among the registrants attending from eight surrounding states.

Bob Strange (Lubbock,) District Chair of the Youth Exchange Committee, reported in August that 9 Youth Exchange students arrived from 9 different countries to spend the academic year in 9 different hosting communities in the District. Ten of our youth departed for similar experiences in 10 communities scattered over 3 continents.

One Rotary Foundation scholar arrived in August, 1996 to spend a year studying at Texas Tech. She was Olga Vasilyeva from Irkutsk, Russia and was sponsored by the Rotary Club of Irkutsk, District 5010.

Governor Sentell established several goals that he took action to accomplish during the 1996-97 year. Specific attention was devoted to the reorganization of several district projects, bolstering the four avenues of service, and emphasizing the Rotary Foundation and the programs established by R.I. President Giay. To pursue those goals Governor Sentell assembled an outstanding group of district Rotarians to insure their achievement. His Area Representatives were Don Cumpton (Hereford,) Byron Edwards (Lubbock,) Mike Gardner (Canadian,) Rick Grogan (Lamesa,) Henry Janhsen (Amarillo East,) R. A. “Bob” Johnson (Pampa,) R. M. “Mert” Keeney (Dumas,) Jim Millsap (Denver City,) Doris Reding (Levelland,) Rick Riddle (Plainview,) Joe Sentell (Snyder,) Mike Tandy (Odessa,) and Ken Winkles (Pecos.)

District committees were headed by the following Rotarians: Rollin Swanson (Snyder) - District Secretary; Ricky Bowman (Sweetwater) - District Treasurer; Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock) and Ted Holder (Levelland) - District Conference Chairs; Kevin G. McMahon (Lubbock) - District Conference Comptroller; W. L. Goble (Lubbock) - District Insurance; PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo) - Nominations; Jon Oden (Amarillo) - Resolutions; PDG Ed Self (Plainview) - Finance; PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa) - Bylaws; PRID Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) - PolioPlus; PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock) - District Apple Orchard; Margaret Lutherer (Lubbock) - Public Relations; PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) - Wheel of Fame Nominations; and DGN J. B. Roberts (Plainview) - On to Glasgow and Rose Parade Float Promotion.

District Committees that addressed the Four Avenues of Service where chaired by PDG Don Williams (Odessa) - Club Service; PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo,) Mike Graves (Plainview,) and J. David Mims (Midland) - Membership Development; Homer Anderson (Snyder) - Club Bulletins and Awards; Joe H. Dominey (Midland) - Community Service; Wynon Mayes (Canyon) - Vocational Service; Ted Holder (Levelland) - International Service and Lannie Lee ( Snyder) - World Community Service.

Four very active Service to Youth Committees were appointed. Bob Strange (Lubbock) was chair of Youth Exchange and was assisted by Diana Hubbard (Lubbock,) Jennifer Shirey (Metro Lubbock,) Mike Tandy (Odessa,) Jackie Finkner (Lubbock,) and Kerry Gilmore (Lubbock.) The two RYLA committees were chaired as follows: Lee George (Big Spring) - Boys’ RYLA; Linda Conway (Big Spring) - Girls’ RYLA; and Claudia Heathington (O’Donnell) - Girls’ RYLA Camp Director. The third Committee, Diabetic Camp, was chaired by Barry Orr (Lubbock.) The Interact chairman was Layne Myatt (Dimmitt.)

PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) chaired the District Friendship Exchange program, and Howard Wilkerson (Canyon) was chair for Recreational and Vocational Fellowships.

PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo) was chair of the Rotary Foundation and the Foundation Permanent Fund. He worked with the following committee chairs: PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa) - Benefactors and Bequests; PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West) - Matching Grants; Dr. Kenneth Ketner (Lubbock) - Ambassadorial Scholarships; Lilia Escajeda (Amarillo East) - Group Study Exchange; Jennifer Shirey (Metro Lubbock) - GSE Team Leader; and Beth Duke (Amarillo West) - Alumni Coordinator.

A real milestone was reached on September 5, 1996 when 50 Paul Harris Fellow awards were presented to members of the Rotary Club of Amarillo. This brought their total PFH awards to 155. Several members received their second award and one couple, PDG Doyle and Doris Moore each received their sixth multiple PHF award.

Governor Sentell chaired the first meeting of his District Advisory Committee in Lubbock on Sept. 7, 1996. Topics on the agenda included a report by Marilyn Ault, chair District Finance Committee in 1995-96, RYLA reorganization, the new District Leadership Plan, and an up-date of the district by-laws. Rotary International was encouraging districts to adopt the new organizational plan which authorized Governors to appoint multiple assistant governors to assist them with administrative duties, particularly those related to attending club assemblies and the official club visits. During the year much discussion took place concerning this substantial reorganization plan and it was adopted with implementation to take place during the 1997-98 Rotary year.

Lilia Escajeda reported that the Group Study Exchange team departed for District 1040 in England Sept. 13, 1996. The Rotarian team leader was Jennifer Shirey (Metropolitan Lubbock.) Team members were Marla Turrentine (Levelland,) Steve Kauffman (Lubbock,) and Maria Douglas (Big Spring.)

The First Applebutter Festival was held in Idalou on Sept. 21. This was a cooperative effort sponsored by the four Rotary Clubs of Lubbock. Music, entertainment, concession stands vending a variety of products, and a raffle kept the crowds and the Lubbock Rotarians busy that day. District Apple Orchard chair PDG Cliff Breaud reported that a check for $6,200 was given to the South Plains Food Bank for the support of the orchard as a results of this affair.

In the latter part of September, 1996 Governor Sentell, DGN J. B. Roberts (Plainview,) and PDGs Moore, Williams, Breaud, McLaughlin, LaBarr and Lewis, all accompanied by their spouses, journeyed to Denver, Colorado for the 1996 Zone 25 - 26 Institute. District 5730 was in Zone 26 which was composed of 11 districts. All districts in Zone 25 were represented at the Institute as well. This important Rotary meeting was designed to provide training for DGNs, keep PDGs current on the affairs of Rotary, and afford opportunities for fun and fellowship.

An interesting bit of Zone politics occurred during this Rotary year. The Zone nominating committee selected PDG Ron Burton (Norman, Oklahoma) from a slate of candidates as their choice for Director of Zone 26 for 1998-2000. Their recommendation was reported at the September, 1996 Zone Institute in Denver. One of the candidates, Ray A. Kneggs, Sr. (District 5810, Rowlett) challenged the choice. Club presidents throughout Zone 26 settled the issue by ballot in the Spring, 1997 by electing the choice of the Zone 26 Nominating Committee.

The late PDG Marshall Formby (Plainview) was honored in Plainview in Sept. when the new Marshall Formby State Jail was dedicated. Sharleen Formby Rhoads was there along with a large group of state, regional, and local dignitaries. Marshall served as District 5730’s Governor in 1973-74 and again during 1975 after Governor Emil Prohl (Tahoka) died.

The Levelland Rotary Club was recognized in the October issue of The Rotarian for their club project, “Take Our Daughters to Work Day.” Club President Gene Parkinson was commended for the club’s efforts in taking this positive step of being of service to youth in their community.

An old tradition was revived by two Rotary clubs in the top of the district in October. Borger club president Carl Chilton bussed his club members to Pampa. Club president Curt Beck and members of the Pampa Rotary club served a hosts for a joint meeting of the two clubs.

PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo,) District Foundation chair reported that the annual District Rotary Foundation Seminar and Dinner was hosted by the Rotary Clubs of Big Spring and held at Howard College on November 9, 1996. The Seminar was an afternoon affair and all aspects of the Rotary Foundation were treated by an array of speakers. The seminar resource person was PDG Ron Burton (Norman, Oklahoma,) who was also an incoming Director of R. I. PDG Burton was the featured speaker at the dinner that evening. Twenty-six Rotarians representing 16 clubs attended the seminar and 59 Rotarians and guests attended the dinner.

Governor Sentell noted in December that Willmon L. White, a former resident of Big Spring, Texas was named General Manager of the Rotary Foundation. He continued to be Editor-in-Chief of The Rotarian. Will, a 27 year staff member of Rotary International and member of the Evanston Rotary Club, was made an honorary member of the Big Spring Club.

Bob Strange (Lubbock,) chair of the District Youth Exchange project and members of his committee conducted interviews on November 16th with students living in the district who wanted to participate in short term and long term visits abroad during the summer of 1997 and the 1997-98 academic year. The interviews were conducted in Lubbock with the 10 out-bound applicants who applied, 6 for long term exchanges (5 accepted,) and 4 for summer exchanges (3 accepted.)

Governor Sentell reported that at the end of November, 1996 there were 2623 members in the District’s 53 Rotary Clubs. Pecos, Floydada, and Lockney were the top clubs in attendance that month.

On December 14, 1996 the District 5730 Nominating Committee, chaired by PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo,) recommended John Heetland (Amarillo West) as their choice for District Governor for 1998-99. John, active in district work for 20 years, was unanimously elected four months later at the 1997 District Conference held in Lubbock.

During December, 1996 PDG Doyle Moore, chair of the District Rotary Foundation posted two newsletters to club presidents regarding the Foundation. The first one explained the 60% - 40% SHARE program of R.I. and requested input from club presidents on how the 60% SHARE of funds credited to the District should be allocated: Humanitarian, Educational, or International Partnership categories. His second newsletter that month reminded clubs that their Foundation contributions credit balances would expire 30 June, 1997 and urged immediate action in two areas: first, that clubs use their credits as matching funds to promote more PHFs and sustaining members, and second, that members with individual credit balances transfer them to other club members to help them achieve the status of a PHF. In both instances PDG Moore stressed that credit balances be used in a manner that would generate additional funds for the Foundation.

Ken Ketner (Lubbock,) chair of the District Ambassadorial Scholarship Committee reported in January that Alice Renee Sneary was awarded the scholarship. She was sponsored by the Dalhart Rotary Club. The award was to be used during the academic year 1997-98 at the University of Cambridge in England.

The second meeting of the Governor’s Advisory Committee was held in Lubbock on Jan. 9, 1997. Questions had previously been raised concerning the financial support of the Apple Orchard project and whether it was in fact an official district project. The meeting was devoted to a discussion of the positions of the South Plains Food Bank, the District Apple Orchard Committee, and District 5730. Discussions led to clarification and guidelines. The orchard, a division of the South Plains Food Bank in Lubbock, was officially adopted as a District project in January, 1997. The Rotary Club of Odessa donated $1500 to the orchard and PDG Cliff Breaud reported that they became the 8th club in the district that became a 100% participant in the project.

At the end of February the Lockney Rotary Club was cited for having been in the Attendance Top 10 list every month during the year. Big Spring and Floydada were not far behind, making the list 7 times out of the 8 months reported. Greater Odessa was the District leader for February with 93% of their members attending club meetings.

International Service chair Ted Holder (Levelland) and World Community Service chair Lannie Lee (Snyder) had another great year with projects in Mexico. Their committees raised over $5,000 which was matched by the District and earmarked for current and future projects in cooperation with the Rotary Club of Madera in District 4110. The WCS committee bought $2500 worth of school supplies that were delivered to Madera by 9 Rotarians from 5 clubs in our District. In conference with Madera Rotarians plans were laid to put a water well near Creel, continue construction of a cafeteria/meeting room north of Madera, and get clearance from Mexican officials to deliver 300 school desks and food for 20,000 children and 10,000 Tarahumara Indians. Governor Sentell was hopeful that a matching grant program could be established that might encourage more clubs in the district to become involved in the W.C.S. arena.

DGN J. B. Roberts and Ramona attended the Rotary International Assembly in Anaheim, California March 7 - 14, 1997. They met with 517 other incoming governors from 154 countries for a one week intensive training session concerning most of the aspects of Rotary and their forthcoming responsibilities. On March 21st they joined 43 incoming club presidents from the District at the annual President-Elect Training Seminar, PETS, in Dallas for three more days of Rotary training. Others from the District attending PETS included faculty members PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo,) PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West,) and PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa.) Governor Sentell served as Assistant Sergeant-at-Arms.

The Rotary Club of Amarillo completed a novel project designed to honor their Paul Harris Fellows and Benefactors. The 100+ names were placed in a hat, four were drawn, and those Rotarians and their spouses were treated to a “Gourmet Dinner” at the home of Ross and Hazel Kelley Wilson on the evening of March 17, 1997. The meal was prepared by George Lokey and a dozen other members of the club provided chauffeured limousines, valet, butler, maid, and dinner arrangements at the elegant and formal affair.

The Group Study Exchange team from District 1040 arrived on March 29, 1997 and began their tour of our district in Plainview. Other scheduled stops included Amarillo, Midland, Odessa, Big Spring, and Lubbock. Their tour ended with an appearance at the District Conference in Lubbock in early May. The team was led by Rotarian Milton Frary (Castleford, England.) Team members, dubbed “The Dream Team,” included Andrew Tunstall (Leeds,) David Wright (Bradford,) Emma Harris (Leeds,) and Victoria Haslam (Oldham.)

The District Assembly was held on the campus of South Plains College in Levelland April 19, 1997. Governor Marvin Sentell convened the meeting then turned it over to DGN J. B. Roberts (Plainview) who proceeded to outline his plans for the year, presented his proposed budget, explained how the new administrative organization of the District involving 8 assistant governors would affect clubs, and then sent those in attendance to the 8 group workshops that he had commissioned. The assembly reconvened for lunch where Lee Weldon Stephenson, a professor at South Plains College, was the featured speaker. The afternoon was devoted to descriptions of each of the 9 district projects and how clubs could become involved in them. Attendance at the Assembly set a new district record with 200 registering for the conference representing 37 clubs. Thirty-six Rotarians from across the district were involved in presenting the programs.

In his April Rotary Foundation Newsletter, PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo) pointed out that district Rotarians had contributed $43,170 in General Giving through March, 1997. He also noted that there were 78 Benefactors of the Foundation and urged members to seriously consider becoming involved in that program.

Governor Sentell opened the 40th Annual District 5730 Conference at the Holiday Inn Lubbock Plaza on May 1, 1997 and it continued through May 4th. The four Rotary Clubs of Lubbock served as hosts and their members worked hard to insure its success. Registration totaled 368 including Rotarians and guests. Thirty-six of the District’s 53 clubs were represented. Preliminary reports showed that the financial aspects of the conference were less than $1,000 below revenue.

Conference chairman Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock) and co-chairman Ted Holder (Levelland) worked with the following Lubbock Rotarians to stage the extravaganza: Beverly Thetford - In-House Services and Registration; Kevin McMahon - Treasurer; David Jones and Patrick Murfee - Food Services; Margaret Lutherer - Publicity/Special Events; Dean Lewis - Transportation; Ron Huckeby, Patricia Collins Davis, Carl Chilton, Winslow Hill and George Keeling - Sergeants-at-Arms; PDG J. Davis Armistead - Aide to the International President’s Representative; Betty Lou Blumrosen, Donna Eagan, and Virgil Barber - Tour Coordinators; Sharon Rousseau - Decorations; and Marjan Wilkins - Conference Secretary and Registration.

On Thursday afternoon, May 1st, Julie Sentell hosted the spouses of PDG’s at the home of Margaret Lutherer for tea while Governor Sentell chaired a meeting of his Advisory Council where future planning was conducted. That evening the Sentells hosted the PDGs at a dinner where R.I. President Giay’s Special Representative to the conference Gary Giersch and spouse Phyllis, was presented. Down the hall DGN J. B. Roberts and Ramona entertained the incoming assistant governors, club presidents and their spouses at a ‘get acquainted’ dinner.

The Special Representative of the President of R.I. was introduced at the opening session by PDG Davis Armistead. He was Garold D. “Gary” Giersch, PDG from District 5220 and a member of the Rotary club of Madera, California. He was accompanied by his spouse, Phyllis. Gary was a civil engineer, president of his company, involved in his community, and active on every level of Rotary.

The District Governor Nominee, J. B. Roberts (Plainview.) was presented, the District Governor Nominee Designate John Heetland (Amarillo West) was introduced, and PDG Bob Lewis (Big Spring) gave an overview of the history of District 5730.

The first plenary session featured an address by Dr. David Freed whose message centered on how Rotarians can become involved in rural health care initiatives. Larry Johnson (Odessa) followed with a presentation on how Rotarians can lend “A Helping Hand.”

The Friday luncheon was chaired by PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo,) featured a call to order by the four Rotary Clubs of Lubbock, contained an introduction of the Group Study Exchange team from District 1040 in England, and was addressed by John T. Montford, Chancellor of the Texas Tech System.

A memorable report was made by Carolyn Lanier, retired Executive Director of the South Plain Food Bank, entitled “How Rotary Makes a Difference: The Apple Orchard Story.” John Gilliam (Metro Lubbock,) and Doris Reding (Levelland) followed with recommendations on “Service Above Self: New Ways to Serve.” That evening the Greater Lubbock Rotary Club hosted one of their famous shrimp boils, complete with a live band and entertainment provided by Maurice Courville, International Cajun Joke-telling Champion. The club conducted a raffle for a Chevrolet Tahoe and raised $4200 for the District Apple Orchard project.

Saturday morning opened with a State of the District address by Governor Sentell, a report on the Council on Legislation by PRID Ralph McLaughlin, balloting for the district’s representative to the next Council on Legislation, and a consideration of resolutions recommended by Jon Oden (Amarillo.) After the break, Preston Lewis, President of the Western Writers of America and associated with the Texas Tech Library, entertained the audience with a story he had researched entitled, “Bluster’s Last Stand.”

Saturday’s Luncheon was highlighted by introductions of visiting Youth Exchange students by Youth Exchange Committee chair Bob Strange (Lubbock,) a speech by Special Representative Gary Giersch, and presentation of Rotary International’s “Service Above Self” award to Dr. Cheri Sparks (Big Spring.) Ted Holder (Levelland) announced that PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo) was elected as delegate to the 1998 Council On Legislation and that PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock) was elected as alternate delegate. PRID Ralph and Billye McLaughlin named grand daughters Jenni and Anna McLaughlin as Paul Harris Fellows and PDG Doyle Moore, District Foundation Director, made the award presentations.

Saturday afternoon’s plenary sessions contained reports by PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo) who reviewed District Foundation activities, Lee George (Big Spring) and Claudia Heathington (O’Donnell) concerning the new location of the RYLA camps to Capitan, New Mexico, and Dudley Faver (Lubbock) on Rotaract.

The Governor’s banquet was held Saturday evening at the Ranching Heritage Center, Texas Tech University. Barbecue was on the menu, Special Representative Gary Giersch extended R. I. President Giay’s greetings, and the crowd was entertained by trick roper Brice Chapman and the Blue Prairie Band.

Sunday morning’s All Faith Memorial Service and Necrology was led by Pastor Paul Jantzen (Lubbock,) a brunch was served and the 40th District Conference concluded as the group sang “Auld Lang Syne.”

Additional awards presented at the conference went to Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock) and Ted Holder (Levelland) who were named Co-Rotarians of the Year. Clubs recognized for outstanding achievement included Kermit, Amarillo East, Big Spring, and Southwest Lubbock. Outstanding club bulletin awards were presented to editors Frank Duckworth (Lockney,) Bill Blackburn (Childress,) Jackie Finkner (Metropolitan Lubbock,) and Jeff Melton (Odessa.)

Four clubs in the district qualified for the 1996-97 Presidential Citation Award for their accomplishments in the Four Avenues of Service: Big Spring, Greater Big Spring, Odessa, and Tahoka.

PDG Charles Beil and Joan (Big Spring) led a delegation of 10 Rotarians and spouses to District 2390 in Sweden in early June, 1997 on a Friendship Exchange visit. Joining the Beils were Hayes and Dorothy Stripling (Big Spring,) PDG Doyle Moore and Doris (Amarillo,) Kathy Cornett (Amarillo) and Steve Cornett (Canyon,) Barbara Miller (Amarillo) and Beth Duke (Amarillo West.) The Moores and Cornetts traveled to the International Convention in Glasgow after their Sweden visit ended. Sixteen travelers from Sweden were expected to visit District 5730 in September, 1998.

Lynn Simpson (Greater Big Spring) was the Friendship Exchange leader that headed a group of nine Rotarians and spouses who visited District 9270 in South Africa June 3 - June 17, 1997. Lynn was joined by Robert and Lea Covington (Odessa,) William and Sarilyn Black (Midland,) Rollie and Jeri Hyde (Plainview,) and Michael and Ingrid Graves (Plainview.) They began their visit by attending the District 9270 Conference in Durban, toured Hluhluwe Game Reserve and Lake St. Lucia in Shakaland, and made stops in Greytown, Estcourt and Scottburgh. Memorable impressions included the exotic wildlife, the beautiful landscape, the schools in which much was accomplished with very little, and the people’s friendliness and determination to make the “New South Africa” work.

Bill and Sarilyn Black arrived four weeks early, rented a car, and toured Johannesburg, Petoria, Kruger Park and Cape Town. The Covingtons joined the Blacks in Cape Town one week before the exchange started. Lynn arrived in South Africa a week early where he met friends in Johannesburg from a previous Group Study Exchange visit to District 5730. Lynn reported that the South Africans might possibly return the Friendship Exchange visit in the Spring, 1999.

As a part of R.I. President Luis Giay’s focus on programs for “New Generations,” Governor Sentell pushed for clubs to organize Interact and Rotaract clubs in the district. He was pleased to report that clubs in Amarillo sponsored the organization of a new Interact Club at Palo Duro High School, bringing the number of clubs in the district to three. Dimmitt and Southwest Lubbock were the other clubs sponsoring Interact clubs in their respective communities. Dudley Faver (Lubbock) helped organize a Rotaract Club at Texas Tech.

The Rotary Club of Sweetwater sponsored the organization of the Snyder Rotary Club in 1947. On the evening of June 7, 1997 Snyder club president Brandy Hickman presided over the celebration of the Snyder club’s 50th anniversary. It was a gala affair that was held at the Snyder Country Club.

A major change in the operation of the Boys’ RYLA Camp occurred during this year. Lee George (Big Spring) assumed the chairmanship and organized a new approach for this district project. Boys’ RYLA was held for the first time at its new location at the Lone Tree Bible Camp outside Capitan, New Mexico on June 9 - 14, 1997. There were 57 young men from 31 sponsoring clubs in attendance. The activities directed by the 12 Rotary volunteers included workshops on values, free enterprise, leadership, and team work coupled with sports, cookouts, and fellowship. The John Ben Sheppard Public Leadership Institute’s Student Leadership Forum, a program of the UT Permain Basin College in Odessa, was substantially involved in the program. A speech competition was held and the two winners were awarded a trip to the District Conference that was held in Ruidoso, New Mexico May 1 - 3, 1998.

The International Institute and International Convention was held in Glasgow, Scotland June 13-18, 1997. PDG Doyle Moore and PRID Ralph McLaughlin attended the Institute then joined DGN J. B. Roberts and Ramona (Plainview) and a sizable delegation of incoming club presidents, PDGs, and club members from the District. A partial list of those attending included Morris Moreland (Amarillo,) Steve Cornett (Canyon,) Kathy Cornett (Amarillo,) Bill Scott (Amarillo West,) Lon Miller (Greater Lubbock,) and Cal Brints (Metropolitan Lubbock) and their spouses. While there, they all ate haggis.

In his end of the year report to Rotary International Governor Sentell commended four areas of service that were most active in the District: Youth Exchange, Interact Clubs, World Community Service, and Friendship Exchange. Problem areas continued to be the ones cited by previous governors: membership growth, Foundation giving, and the need for club fund raisers.

Club membership was 2,596 at the beginning of this year and declined to 2,573 as of the end of June, 1997, a net loss of 23 members. Attendance figures showed that Floydada continued to lead the district (93%,) followed by Greater Odessa (90%,) Seagraves (88%,) Pecos (86%,) and Plainview (85%.)

Governor Sentell described his year as a fulfilling and enlightening experience citing the opportunities of visiting the district’s 53 clubs, the enjoyment of the Calgary International Convention, witnessing the involvement of clubs and individual Rotarians in their communities, and grasping the significance of the possibilities for service that are attainable on all levels through Rotary. He was particularly pleased that two thorny issues were successfully resolved. The first was the specter of change that confronted the adoption of a new district leadership program. Established procedures, ritual, and traditions were carefully examined and resulted in the introduction of a plan for the appointment of eight assistant governors whose functions were to aid the governor in administrative areas. The new plan took effect July 1, 1997.

The second issue concerned whether the Apple Orchard had ever been officially adopted as a district project and the extent to which the district was committed to fund the operation. A firm understanding was reached between the leadership of District 5730 and the South Plains Food Bank as to their respective roles in the operation and promotion of the Apple Orchard. The project was officially adopted as a District project. The Food Bank agreed to accept all responsibility for the orchard and to furnish the personnel and equipment necessary for its maintenance and growth. District 5730 agreed to promote the orchard and to do its best to raise funds and supply both leadership and volunteers as needed. Governor Sentell was excited about the importance of this project and saw evidence that the efforts of PDG Cliff Breaud, PDG Jim Cook, and Howard Mercer, with substantial help from PRID Ralph McLaughlin, would carry the Apple Orchard program to a higher level.

The Rotary Club of Greater Lubbock showed its support for the Apple Orchard in a big way. At the Lubbock District Conference the club raffled off a vehicle at their 5th annual Shrimp Boil. Club President Brad Moran reported that the Tahoe Benefit Drawing was profitable and on June 30, 1997 sent Governor Sentell a check for $4,312.50, funds that ultimately were presented to the South Plains Food Bank and earmarked for the Apple Orchard.

PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo) reported that contributions to the Rotary Foundation totaled $90,918.16 during the 1996-97 Rotary year. The General Fund received $85,318.16 and the balance of $5,600 went into the Permanent Fund. The District gained 27 new Benefactors of the Rotary Foundation. New Paul Harris Fellows totaled 174 and there were 54 new Sustaining Members added to the roster of Foundation contributors.

CHAPTER X

“The First Ever”

July 1 – February 28, 1998


The year began with a big celebration in Roswell, New Mexico. In early July thousands were drawn there to rekindle conspiracy theories that the Air Force had covered up alien sightings for 50 years. Not to be outdone, NASA landed the Pathfinder on Mars and the Dow Industrial Average hit the 8,000 mark on July 16, 1997. After a nationwide hunt serial killer Andrew Cunanan was found dead on a yacht at Miami, Florida ending a mystery surrounding the death of fashion designer Gianni Versace. William Brennan, Supreme Court Justice died on July 26th.

In resent years the image of the Dallas Cowboys became somewhat tarnished by antics of some of the players. In August it was the coach’s turn. Barry Switzer was arrested at DFW airport for carrying a gun in his luggage. The Teamster’s union called a strike against United Parcel Service delaying package deliveries and delighted the U.S. Postal Service. Timothy McVeigh was sentenced to death for the Oklahoma City bombing. Fans of Elvis Presley commemorated the 20th anniversary of his death, SAT math scores gained some ground, and the drilling rig count in the district reached a 20 year high. Russia’s MIR space station continued to experience computer problems affecting its life support and navigation systems causing questions to be raised regarding the wisdom of continuing the presence of U.S. astronauts on board. The world was stunned by the death of Diana Spencer, formerly the Princess of Wales, and mother of a future King of England. Her death occurred in a car crash on August 31, 1997 in a Paris tunnel.

In September, both sadness and admiration prevailed upon reports that Mother Teresa, born Agnes Gonxha Bojaxhiu in Macedonia, died of heart failure at the age of 87. Her life was a case study of service to others and her work was expected to continue through the worldwide order that she founded, the Missionaries of Charity. While the world mourned both of these women, factions opposed to peace in both the Middle East and the Balkans continued to exert their influence. Famine was sweeping North Korea. In Washington, DC the Democrats and Republicans loudly heralded the need for each other to reform their campaign financing tactics. Bob Bullock’s announcement that he would not seek reelection to the post of Lieutenant Governor of the State of Texas scrambled the political eggs in Austin. Campaigning for statewide offices began in earnest during the fall, 1997.

For years, Japan denied U.S. ships the same freedoms in her ports that Japanese ships enjoyed in American ports and negotiations did not resolve that problem. In October, 1997 The U.S. Maritime Commission finally got Japan’s attention by refusing to let Japanese ships dock at, or leave, U.S. ports. The issue was suddenly resolved. At home other issues such as abortion, global warming, physician assisted suicide, and genetic engineering to improve the human race, were far from settled. Questions also remained unanswered regarding the Whitewater issue, Paula Jones’ accusation of sexual harassment by President Clinton, and improprieties of fund raising by both political parties.

In October, 1997, the Florida Marlins (age: 5 years) won the World Series, the president of China, Jiang Zemin was saluted, wined, and dined at the White House by President Clinton, and investors in markets worldwide rode a spooky roller coaster the week before Halloween. Texas voters approved an amendment to the state constitution permitting home equity loans and there was a mad scramble among in-state and out of state lenders to get in the business. The eleventh Presidential Library, a monument to the 41st President of the United States, George Bush, was dedicated November 6th at Texas A&M University. Ironically, President Bush’s old nemesis, Iraq’s Sadam Hussein, was still in power and defying the U.N. and the U.S by prohibiting weapon inspection teams access to weapons sites, expelling U.S. members of those teams, and threatening to fire on U.S. surveillance aircraft. President Clinton rattled U.S. sabers but lacked support from key allies for military action.

A woman in Iowa gave birth to seven babies in November and there was an outpouring of donations and sympathy from across America. By the end of the year the economies of several Asian nations crashed and their leaders went to the International Monetary Fund, red faced and hat-in-hand for a bail out. “El Nino” was predicted to substantially increase rainfall in California and the southern parts of the U.S.

In January the Denver Broncos upset the Green Bay Packers in the Super Bowl, a game that only briefly interrupted media coverage of the Monica Lewinsky – President Clinton sex scandal. While America focused on the notion of presidents having sex with White House interns, President Clinton and Sadam Hussein of Iraq appeared to move to the brink of war. A last minute agreement was negotiated by the Secretary General of the UN in which Hussein agreed to permit UN arms inspectors to resume their duties in Iraq. The movie “Titanic” ruled the box offices during the early part of 1998.

On July 1, 1997, Glen W. Kinross became Rotary International’s President. He was a 37 year member of the Rotary Club of Hamilton, Brisbane, Australia. His theme for the year was “Show Rotary Cares - for your community, for our world, for its people.” He urged the 1,200,000 Rotarians in 28,000 clubs in 155 countries to focus their attention on the problems of poverty, illiteracy, and child abuse. During the first half of his year he maintained a heavy travel schedule to champion his theme. His Rotary International Convention was scheduled for Indianapolis, Indiana in June, 1998.

District 5730 provided strong leadership to support President Kinross when J. B. Roberts of Plainview was named Governor of the district. Governor Roberts was born in Quanah, Texas, graduated from Plainview High School, earned a BBA degree from Baylor University, and served as a commissioned officer in the U.S. Air Force (OSI and SAC) during the Korean war, 1951-53. He returned to Plainview where he worked for the New York Fire Insurance Company as a special agent for several years before establishing J. B. Roberts & Associates Real Estate, Inc. in 1963. From then until 1992 he was involved in real estate, property and farm management and commercial construction. He remained semi-active in the business after his retirement in 1992.

The Governor married Ramona Faye Curry of Plainview and they raised two sons, Randall and Drury, and a daughter, Sarah. Their children delighted them with six grandchildren. All family members were active participants in the church, social, and civic affairs of Plainview including scouting, school activities, and community fine arts. J. B. was an officer or director of many civic groups including the Chamber of Commerce, Plainview Country Club, Industrial Foundation, Airport Board, the United Way, Prairie House Nursing Home, Buckner Baptist Children’s Home, Lonetree Recovery Center, Salvation Army, and the Crisis Pregnancy Center. He was a member of the Plainview First Baptist Church for more than 50 years and rendered many years of service in capacities ranging from Chairman of Deacons to Sunday School Teacher and everything in between those positions. He served as Chairman of the Building Committee for the Family Life Building for the First Baptist Church. Wayland Baptist University benefited from his leadership as Chairman of the Executive Committee and Chairman of the Board of Trustees. He was active in many of the professional associations of his business.

Other interests included hunting, fishing, and flying his Beechcraft Bonanza around the patch. A study of genealogy and history led to memberships in the Sons of the American Revolution, Sons of the Republic of Texas, The Jamestown Society, American Legion, and Sons of Confederate Veterans. Everyone knew that J.B. played golf, but it was not one of his hobbies - it was serious business.

All of the above is presented to show the depth of experience and magnitude of ability that Rotary continued to tap for its leadership. Governor Roberts brought to the office a 39 year affiliation with Rotary, having joined the Plainview Rotary Club in 1958. He served as chair of many committees, attended the London International Convention in 1978, was on the Board of Directors, and functioned in each officer position in the club. J.B. and Ramona attended the International Convention in Taipei, Taiwan in June, 1994. He served as president of his club in 1994-95 and the District took note. In addition to having a banner year, the club’s membership increased by 51 Rotarians, growing to 118 members. The Rotary Club of Plainview received a Presidential Citation Award, was named “Outstanding Club of the Year” and President Roberts was named “Rotarian of the Year” at the Pampa District Conference in 1995 by Governor Chuck LaBarr. J. B. and Ramona were Multiple Paul Harris Fellows, Benefactors of the Rotary Foundation, and held Arch Klumph Awards. Both of their sons were Paul Harris Fellows and Benefactors. J. B. was a member of 5 Rotary International Fellowships: Golfing, Flying Rotarians, Rotary Heritage & History, Genealogy, and the Paul Harris - 711 Club.

On January 11, 1996 PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa) reported that the District Nominating Committee had selected J. B. Roberts of Plainview to be Governor of District 5730 during the 1997 - 1998 year. Although confirmation was not scheduled until the 1996 Amarillo District Conference in May, 1996, J. B. hit the ground running. The next 18 months were spent in a whirlwind of complete immersion in the affairs of Rotary on the club, district, zone, and international levels. As DGD, he observed and participated in the district committee work of both RYLA camps, Youth Exchange, World Community Service, the Foundation Seminars and Paul Harris Dinners, Group Study Exchange, the Apple Orchard, and the Ambassadorial Scholarship programs. He attended DGN Sentell’s (Snyder) District Assembly, and DG Moore’s District Conference. During the year 1996-97 as DGN, J.B. continued his involvement with all District projects, began putting his team together, and pursued his Rotary training. With Ramona by his side he attended the 1996 summer RYLA camps, the 4 day Zone 25 - 26 meeting in Denver held in September, 1996, and sat in on the Rotary Foundation Seminar and Paul Harris Dinner held in Big Spring in November. March, 1997 was busy for he participated in Rotary International’s two-day celebration of the Rotary Foundation’s 50th anniversary in Los Angeles, and the 8 day Rotary International Assembly held in Anaheim, California March 7-14, 1997, met the Group Study Exchange Team from England in Plainview, and led the District’s Presidents-Elect to the three day PETS meeting held in Dallas. During the Spring, 1997 DGN Roberts began a series of meetings with his incoming Assistant Governors that he recruited earlier in the year. The topic for these meetings, of course, was the new District Leadership Plan. Governor Roberts had special insight regarding the plan, having visited personally with the developer of the concept at the International Assembly in Anaheim, Past RI Director Donald Kwait. Please refer to Appendix XIII for a detailed description of this innovative organizational structure.

DGN Roberts conducted one of the memorable District Assemblies held in Levelland on April 19, 1997. Plenty of “first evers” occurred at this meeting: a new attendance record was established when 200 attended the meeting, the new District Leadership Plan was presented, all eight of the new incoming Assistant Governors were introduced, and 15 of 22 members of DGN Roberts’ District Advisory Committee were present. Incoming Assistant Governor Phelps Blume of Levelland chaired local hosting duties and was aided by many members of both of the Levelland Rotary Clubs. Thirty-seven of the district’s 53 clubs were represented at the assembly and the assistant governors vowed make-up sessions for those clubs that were absent. Eight group sessions were held for incoming officers and committee chairs during the morning, and each of the district’s 9 projects was described in detail that afternoon. Some 36 Rotarians from all parts of the district took an active part in the presentations. DGN Roberts seemed pleased with the entire affair.

Governor Sentell’s Lubbock District Conference was next on the Roberts’ agenda for the month of May, then they journeyed to Glasgow, Scotland for the International Convention held in June, 1997 where they joined a large group of fellow Rotarians and spouses from the district. They took part in the Boys’ RYLA Camp in late June, and after that it was July 1, 1997, and the governor’s pin was passed from Marvin Sentell to J. B. Roberts in an official ceremony in Plainview. It was time for the new governor to perform his duties.

The 1997-98 year began with the “first ever” official club visits being conducted by Assistant Governors instead of the District Governor. The district had been divided into eight areas and an Assistant Governor was assigned the tasks of conducting administrative work plus club assemblies and official visits with the clubs in his area. The eight Assistant Governors were knowledgeable Rotarians with proven dedication and ability and included:

Area 1 Jack McWhirter (Spearman;)
Area 2 Nory Olay (Childress;)
Area 3 Henry Janhsen (Amarillo East;)
Area 4 Phelps Blume (Levelland;)
Area 5 Dudley Faver (Lubbock;)
Area 6 Joe Don Hancock (Midland;)
Area 7 Scott McLaughlin (Greater Big Spring;)
Area 8 Mike Tandy (Odessa)

These Rotarians conducted club assemblies and addressed each of the 53 clubs regarding district goals, projects, and opportunities in a “first ever” record time, finishing all official visits on September 1, 1997. They worked with the following club officers:

Within the Plainview Rotary Club and the general community of Plainview, Governor Roberts was known as a “delegater.” District 5730 soon learned that Governor Roberts intended for all Rotarians on his team to perform the duties of the responsibility they had accepted. At the 1997 Lubbock District Conference, DGN Roberts distributed his district directory, assembled with the help of son Drury Roberts. The directory proved to be one of the most thorough and informative pieces of work regarding the activities of Rotary in District 5730 to be published. After its distribution, J. B. lived with the telephone, fax machine, internet and U. S. Postal Service urging action by those named to pursue their jobs. It had an effect. Stacey Ream (Plainview,) chair of District Public Relations, distributed an extensive piece of work on who’s in charge, who to call, and how to publicize work being conducted by clubs. PDG Davis Armistead published a “Rotary Speaker’s Bureau,” listing more than 100 Rotarians who would present programs on various aspects of Rotary. All other committees were abuzzzzz.

Guiding the activities in District 5730 where the goals that Governor Roberts had established. These included making the District Leadership Plan work, promoting the 3 F’s: family, fun, and fellowship - getting Rotarians and their families involved together, boosting membership, raising funds for the Rotary Foundation, and emphasizing RI President Glen Kinross’ goals of making a difference where hunger, poverty, and child abuse where concerned. Governor Roberts seemed very serious about achieving these goals and he tapped a talented and dedicated group of Rotarians to pursue those ends. District chairs included: Glenn D. Bickel (Plainview) - Secretary; Rick Riddle (Plainview) - Treasurer; Thaxter D. Price (Lubbock) - Executive Treasurer; Kevin Moseley (Plainview,) Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock) and Fred Chesser (Amarillo East) - District Conference; Jimmy Holmes (Plainview) - Conference Comptroller; Drury B. Roberts (Plainview) - District Directory and Governor’s Newsletters; J. David Mims (Midland) - Insurance; PDG Marvin Sentell (Snyder) - Finance Chairman and Nominations; C. David Cobb (Lubbock) - Co-Chair District Finance; Stacey Ream (Plainview) - Public Relations; DGN John Heetland (Amarillo West) - Rose Bowl Parade RI Float and “On to Indianapolis” RI Convention; PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) - Wheel of Fame Nominations; PDG Don Williams (Odessa) - Resolutions; PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa) - ByLaws; PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo) - Historian; PDG Cliff Breaud (Lubbock, ) Howard Mercer (Southwest Lubbock) and George O. Elle (Lubbock) - Apple Orchard; PDG Ed Self (Plainview) - District Trainer; PDG Davis Armistead (Lubbock) - Speaker’s Bureau; DGN John Heetland (Amarillo West) and Grady Elder, Jr. (Plainview) - District Assembly.

Additional chairs included Art Rousseau (Lubbock) and Larry Driskill (Lubbock) - Club Service; PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo) and Grady Elder, Jr. (Plainview) - Membership Development; PDG Jack Selby (Lubbock) - Attendance; R. M. “Mert” Keeney (Dumas) - Club Bulletins; Curt Beck (Pampa) and Ray Purcell (Lubbock) - Archives; Doris Moore (Amarillo) and Julie Sentell (Snyder) - Club Awards; Scott Morgan (Sweetwater) - Extension; Brad Moran (Lubbock) - Rotary Information and Communications; Steve Moffett (Lubbock) and Bill Sharpley (Lubbock) - Fellowship, Family, and Fun Activities.

Lloyd C. Woods (Plainview) and John R. Skaggs (Plainview) were co-chairs of Community Service. Scott Fanning (Lubbock) handled Rotaract and Interact activities.

Other committees were headed by Cheri R. Sparks (Big Spring) and Wynon Mayes (Canyon) - Vocational Service; Lee George (Big Spring) - Boys’ RYLA; Linda Conway (Big Spring) - Girls’ RYLA; Claudia Heathington (O’Donnell) Girls’ RYLA Camp Director; Barry Orr (Lubbock) - Diabetic Camp; PDG Bill Hubbs (Pecos) and Randall Roberts (Plainview) - Vocational Fellowships; Marilyn Van Petten (Amarillo East) - Mentor Program; and Doris Reding (Levelland) and Pat Davis (Childress) - Literacy.

International Service was chaired by Ted Holder (Levelland.) Others working in that area included: Mike Graves (Plainview) - World Community Service; PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring) - Friendship Exchange; Bob Strange (Lubbock) - Youth Exchange; Jennifer Shirey (Metro Lubbock) - Inbound Student Exchange; David Ring (Odessa) - Outbound Student Exchange; Marci Ryan (Amarillo) - Outbound Student Recruitment & Communications; Randy Brillhart (Perryton) - Interviews; Carl Luckenbach (Lubbock) - Insurance; and Kevin Moseley (Plainview) - Splash Down.

PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo) chaired the District Rotary Foundation Committee. He was assisted by the following Rotarians: PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa) - Benefactors and Bequests; PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West) - Matching Grants; David DeBusk (Plainview) - Ambassadorial Scholarships; Bruce Roberson (Perryton) - Ambassadorial Scholarship Host; Janet Hufnagel Thompson (Southwest Amarillo) - Ambassadorial Scholarship Alumni; Lynn Simpson (Big Spring) - Group Study Exchange; Beth Duke (Amarillo West) - Group Study Exchange Alumni; Harvey Rhoads (Midland) - Paul Harris Fellowship Award; and PRID Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) - PolioPlus.

Governor Roberts and Ramona attended the Girls’ RYLA Camp that was held July 21-26, 1997 at the Lone Tree Bible Ranch in Capitan, New Mexico. Linda Conway (Big Spring) served as committee chair and Claudia Heathington (O’Donnell) directed the camp with assistance from Terri Newton. Linda reported that there were 82 young women in attendance that were treated to a week of seminars on leadership, problem solving, conflict resolution, and fun by the volunteer Rotary staff. Again this year the resources of the John Ben Sheppard Public Leadership Institute of the University of Texas Permian Basin were used in the camp. Camp counselors devoting a week to the camp included Marsha Boren, Jan Foresyth, Patsy Sanders, Brenda Hansler, Beth Duke, Sis Olson, Cynthia Scott, Brenda Shirey, and Cherly Shults.

Barry Orr (Southwest Lubbock,) chair of the Diabetic Camp committee reported that the camp was held at Ceta Glen near Canyon, Texas in July, 1997. Fifty-eight children, ages 7 - 14, attended and learned about their disease under the direction of Dr. Surendra Varma and Dr. Michael Bourgeois and 26 other health professionals from the Texas Tech Health Science Center. Governor Roberts joined DGN John Heetland (Amarillo West) and Howard Wilkerson (Canyon) for a visit to the camp and reported that they were impressed to the point that they wished all Rotarians could witness the events that took place at the camp every year.

The District Finance Committee chaired by PDG Marvin Sentell (Snyder) with help from PDG Ed Self (Plainview) selected a permanent Executive Treasurer for the District, Rotarian Thaxter D. Price, CPA, owner of Price and Company, Certified Public Accountants, of Lubbock. In previous years each governor selected a district treasurer that would be close at hand, but as the financial affairs of the District became more extensive a need arose for continuity and standardization of financial reporting.

Bob Strange (Greater Lubbock,) chair of the District Youth Exchange Committee reported that four students from the district were in Europe for the academic year. Kevin Moseley (Plainview,) chair of Splash Down, District Youth Exchange Committee, hosted a roundtable discussion group at Wayland College in August, 1997 composed of the ten youth exchange students visiting our district. The students discussed their homes, experiences abroad, and delighted their audience. Other adventures planned by Jennifer Shirey (Metro Lubbock,) chair of Inbound Students for the fall included a weekend at a dude ranch at Snyder, Halloween at the Sentells in Snyder, a football weekend at Texas Tech, a bash at the Lake Ransom Canyon Club House, a bar-b-que hosted by the Tahoka club, and trips to the South Plains Mall in Lubbock.

Lynn Simpson (Big Spring,) chair of the Group Study Exchange Committee, reported that Group Study Exchanges had been established as follows:

Spring 1998 - District 4750, Brazil, Rio de Janeiro area. Spring 1999 - District 3850, Philippines, Negros Occ.Iloiln area.
Spring 2000 - District 2490, Israel, the entire country.

Lynn was busy in October, 1997 organizing the selection process for the Brazilian exchange.

Seventeen new Paul Harris Fellows were presented their awards in Plainview in August, 1997. The pity of the occasion was that there were several other donors who could not be present for the ceremony. They were scheduled to receive their awards at a later time.

August 20, 1997 was a special day for a special Rotarian. PDG J. M. “Jimmy” Willson, Jr. (Floydada) was awarded a plaque recognizing his 50 years of perfect attendance. That represented 2,600 consecutive Rotary meetings. Another couple of thousand or so meetings might be added to that, however. For many years Jimmy attended every assembly, institute, seminar, advisory council, inter-city, district convention, anniversary celebration, zone, and R.I. convention held. He made hundreds of speeches to clubs all over the southwest. He was a district mainstay at Legislative Councils. He served two full terms as District Governor, his own in 1963-64 and again in 1965-66 when Jerry Ratcliff (Amarillo) was unable to serve. He became the perennial club secretary of the Floydada Rotary Club, the club that consistently set the standards for attendance in District 5730.

The district paused on August 31, 1997 to observe the death of PDG Bruce Pember (Slaton.) Bruce rendered a lifetime of service to Rotary and was governor of the district in 1960-61, the greatest year for inducting new Rotarians.

An interesting thing happened on the way to the 1997 International Convention. During a lively session on world hunger held at the 1997 International Institute in Glasgow, Scotland, PDG John Tyler (Spicewood, Texas) cited the outstanding work being done at the Breeklove Dehydration Plant in Lubbock and queried the panelist as to why Rotary leadership had not picked up on this concept. Apparently Rotary leadership was listening at that meeting, for later that day PRIP Cliff Dochterman, chair of the Rotary Foundation Board of Trustees, asked PRID Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring) if he thought the project had matured to the point of being a viable entity and if it would be worthwhile for the President of Rotary International to pay a visit to the site. Ralph assured Cliff that it was. Cliff quickly involved RI President Glen Kinross and President-Elect Jim Lacy; Ralph involved DGN J. B. Roberts, and others at the convention. Ralph faxed PDG Breaud (Lubbock) and PDG Jim Cook (Amarillo West) to verify their enthusiasm for the visit. He got immediate replies from them to arrange it. Before the convention ended the stage was set for Rotary’s three top leaders to visit Lubbock and view first hand District 5730’s Apple Orchard, the South Plains Food Bank, and the Breedlove Dehydration Plant.

There was plenty of “first evers” that occurred on September 2-3, 1997 in Lubbock in conjunction with their visit. The meeting of RI’s President, President-Elect, and Foundation Trustee chair to view a district project was unprecedented. PDG Carlo Cortipasse, Area Coordinator for the Alleviation of Poverty and Hunger, PDG Peter Faye, Zone 23 Coordinator, and District 5730’s club and committee leaders also came calling. Due to the planning of the host committee, Governor Roberts, PDG Cliff Breaud, PDG Jim Cook, and PRID Ralph McLaughlin, plus the involvement of the four Rotary clubs in Lubbock, the best possible case for Rotary International’s involvement in projects designed to feed the world’s hungry was made. Receptions, meals, and tours filled the two day affair. President Kinross said that projects such as this one started by the Rotary Club of Lubbock complimented his goal of reducing poverty. President-Elect Lacy said he intended to pursue the same goal during his year. PRIP Dochterman indicated that the Foundation Trustees would be examining future programs of a similar nature. District Rotarians who were associated with the project and the visit were quite pleased.

Governor Roberts held the ‘first ever” District 5730 All Club Meeting at noon on Sept. 3, 1997 and more than 700 Rotarians and guests responded to his invitation, a number rivaled only by Lubbock Intercity Meetings of years gone by. Club president Morris Moreland (Amarillo) called the meeting to order with 80% of the clubs in the district ringing their bells simultaneously. President Kinross opened his remarks by commenting that the crowd sang The Star Spangled Banner much better than Waltzing Matilda. He presented 10 Paul Harris Awards to Rotarians from five clubs then delivered an address that outlined his goals.

The four-day Zone 25-26 meeting was held in San Antonio beginning September 4th and continued through September 7, 1997. Governor Roberts, DGN Heetland, and PDGs Breaud, McLaughlin, Cook, Moore, LaBarr, Williams, Sentell, Tyler, Armistead and their ladies rushed from the Lubbock meeting to attend this important conference which was an up-date of Rotary information, fellowship, and training. Several of our delegates were actively involved in the program of the conference. PDG Cook, Zone 26 Coordinator for the Committee on Poverty and Hunger, moderated a panel composed of four agricultural authorities involved in solving the acute crisis of poverty and hunger, DGN Heetland showed a film on the Breedlove Dehydration Plant and outlined our goals of Rotary involvement in that process, and PDG Breaud manned an apple orchard display booth and provided Lubbock apples to those in attendance. PRID McLaughlin served as moderator at one of the meals and presentations.

The second annual “Apple Butter Festival” was held at Hi Plains Orchard near Idalou on September 6 - 7, 1997. The two day festival, a project sponsored by the four Rotary clubs of Lubbock, featured a variety of live music, square dancing, craft booths, apple harvesting, and apple butter production. There was an abundance of food and an attendance of 8,000 people to eat it. The supply of apple butter was sold out and the District 5730 Apple Orchard received $18,749.39 as a result of the event.

While all of this was going on PDG Charles and Joan Beil, Hayes and Dorothy Stripling, and Ray and Nirmala Reddy, all of Big Spring, were in District 4340 located in Santiago and the south of Chile on a two week Friendship Exchange visit that began on August 31, 1997. This was a return visit for our District. The Chileans rolled out the red carpet for the group, introduced them to two Rotary clubs composed exclusively of women, showed them the most beautiful part of South America, and wined and dined them in splendor. When the exchange ended, the Beils and Striplings traveled to Lima, Peru, the upper Amazon Basin, and the Inca kingdom of Machu Picchu, Ecquador, and the Galapagos Islands. PDG Beil continued to be most supportive of Rotary’s Friendship Exchange program, urging all Rotarians in the District to become involved in it.

Joan Johnson, president of the Odessa Rotary Club, reported that her club recognized and honored the wives of fourteen deceased Rotarians on September 17, 1997. The “first ever” Recognition Service included a brief historical reflection of the club and its accomplishments during the lifetime of each of these past members.

Ted Holder (Levelland,) chair of the District World Community Service Committee reported that a trip to Madera, Arollo Ancho, and Creel, Mexico was made by 8 Rotarians and two spouses September 11 - 14, 1997. The trip was a continuation of projects of long standing in these areas of Mexico. The 10 people traveling in three cars included Lynn Simpson and Maria Douglass (Big Spring,) Noble Wiltsire and PDG Louis Rochester (Odessa,) Ron Pressly and Don Shinn (Greater Odessa,) and Don and Leanne Phillips and Dave and Alma Shuler (Seminole.) The group’s first stop was Chihuahua, Mexico where they purchased $2,294.10 worth of school supplies that were to be supplied to approximately 1,000 students. The supplies were loaded in their cars and distributed in Madera, Arollo Ancho, and Creel over the next two days. The group also examined two badly needed water supply projects in the Arollo Ancho and Creel areas, both of which were destitute. Don Shinn (Greater Odessa) said that several hundred dollars spent on these two water systems would greatly impact the lives of 660 people and supply water to two schools with enrollments of 190 students.

In addition to making official visits to clubs, Governor Roberts continued lines of communication with numerous groups including students selected as “Student of the Month” by Rotary clubs, visiting and outbound Youth Exchange students, and new Rotary club members. Club presidents were reminded of RI’s President Citation Award and urged to meet those qualifications. The Governor was confident that more than 50% of the clubs in the district would qualify.

Stacey Ream (Plainview,) District P.R. chair, reported that a 1997-98 District 5730 All Club Raffle had been established with proceeds going to the Rotary Foundation. Rotarians were to sell $10 tickets for a chance at an eight day trip to London for two.

Curt Beck (Pampa) chaired an ambitious project of securing all Rotary records from clubs, committees, and individual Rotarians to be placed in the archives of the Southwest Collection of Texas Tech University. Ray Purcell (Plainview) worked on this with Curt and PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa) offered his assistance. It was rumored that PDG Jimmy Willson (Floydada) had two file cabinets full of Rotary business dating back to the days of his father’s beginning in Rotary.

Bill Wertz (Plainview) chaired a district project called Gifts for Better Vision and sought eye glasses for shipment to Mexico. Rotary clubs in Mexico, the Red Cross of Mexico and vision professionals in Mexico cooperated to distribute the used eyeglasses to the needy in Mexico.

More great news for the apple orchard occurred at the Farmer Stockman show in Lubbock held October 7-9, 1997. At 10:00 A.M. on October 8th, Dr. George Elle (Lubbock) was presented with a new tractor for the orchard by the Dallas District Director of John Deere. It was a $38,000 low profile tractor, complete with cab, air conditioning, heat, and other bells and whistles. Tractors need to be kept in barns so the Southwest Lubbock Rotary Club adopted a project to build a large pole barn at the orchard site.

PRID Ralph McLaughlin and Billye served as the President of R.I.’s Special Representative to the District 7600 Conference in Williamsburg, Virginia on September 18 - 20, 1997. Ralph was particularly impressed with the fact that in this District there were 6 Rotaract and 39 Interact clubs.

PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo) was selected by the Board of Directors of Lone Star PETS to be the Registrar for the March 27-29, 1998 PETS meeting, a formidable task. He requested that PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo) serve as his co-chairman. Carruth was later given the job of Treasurer for the 1998 PETS conference. Doyle was a busy Rotarian during this year, serving as District Foundation Chair, organizing the November, 1997 District Foundation Seminar and Dinner meeting in Plainview, and representing the District at the January, 1998 Council on Legislation meeting in Delhi, India.

On the evening of October 23, 1997 The Rotary Club of Amarillo was joined by the Rotary Clubs of Amarillo West, Amarillo East, Amarillo South, and Canyon for an all-club celebration of Amarillo’s 80th anniversary of Rotary on the high plains of Texas. It was a flawless event hosted by Amarillo club president Morris Moreland and staged by Sally Manning (Amarillo) and her program committee. Well over 200 Rotarians and guests assembled at the Amarillo Country Club to hear the opening prayer given by Gene Shelburne (Amarillo West,) a message from Governor Roberts, a brief recap of 80 years of Rotary Global History from PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo,) and an entertaining and inspiring presentation from PDG Andy Smallwood, a resident of Pearland, and representing the Rotary Club of Houston, the Amarillo club’s sponsor in 1917. PDG Andy was accompanied by his pretty wife, Anita. Gary Moore (Amarillo West) did his usual outstanding job of elevating spirits by leading singing. Gary Mingus (Amarillo) provided dinner music and accompaniment for the singing. It was a great evening.

 PDG Farris Oden (Amarillo) who was governor of District 573 1972-1973 saddened the Rotary Club of Amarillo on November 13th by tendering his resignation from Rotary. Farris joined Rotary in Pampa in 1932 and rendered 65 years of distinguished service to his clubs, the District, and Rotary International. He was only 92 years of age.

PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo,) chair of the District Rotary Foundation Committee, organized and convened the District 5730 Rotary Foundation Seminar in Plainview at the Country Club on November 15, 1997. An unseasonable blizzard the day before gave Rotarians a good excuse not to attend, but 125 brave souls were on hand on Saturday to learn about Foundation programs at the seminar and later at the dinner. PDG Mike Pinson (Kileen, District 5870,) accompanied by his lovely wife, Mary, served as the seminar resource person and performed at his usual best. All aspects of the Rotary Foundation were covered by presentations delivered by DGN John Heetland (Amarillo West,) PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa,) A.G. Phelps Blume (Levelland,) A.G. Joe Don Hancock (Midland,) A.G. Jack McWhirter (Spearman,) A.G. Mike Tandy (Odessa,) A.G. Scott McLaughlin (Greater Big Spring,) A.G. Nory Olay, M.D. (Childress,) A.G. Dudley Faver (Lubbock,) A.G. Henry Janhsen (Amarillo East,) PDG Paige Carruth (Amarillo,) PDG Ed Self (Plainview,) Lynn Simpson (Big Spring,) David DeBusk (Plainview,) Janet Hufnagel Thompson (Amarillo West,) and Beth Duke (Amarillo West.)

At the Foundation dinner that evening Gary Moore (Amarillo West) reved up excitement with his song leading and PDG Pinson made an inspirational address to a crowd of almost 100. He then joined Governor Roberts, and PDG Moore in awarding many new multiple Paul Harris Fellow pins, Paul Harris Fellow awards, and Benefactor wings. PDG Moore announced that Major Donors to the Foundation had reached eight in the District and included PDG Charles Beil (Big Spring,) Ray Diekemper (Lubbock,) Mrs. Dorothy Garret (Big Spring,) PDG Chuck LaBarr (Pampa,) PRID Ralph McLaughlin (Big Spring,) Mrs. Sharleen Formby Rhoads (Midland,) PDG Louis Rochester (Odessa,) and PDG Don Williams (Odessa.)

Plainview club president Grady Elder, Glenn Bickel, and other Plainview Rotarians did a great job of hosting the seminar. Governor Roberts elaborated on his plan for a new district-wide Foundation fund raiser, a raffle of six trips to London for 8 days: two trips for the winner, two trips for the winning ticket seller, and two trips to the club of the winner. Continental Airlines donated the air travel and the Forte Hotel Corporation donated the rooms in London.

Scott Morgan (Sweetwater,) chair of the District Extension Committee was actively coordinating efforts to develop Rotary Clubs in Clarendon, Quanah, Silverton, Friona, and Stanton.

Lynn Simpson (Big Spring,) chair of the Group Study Exchange Committee announced on November 15th the names of the GSE team going to Rio de Janeiro in District 4750 in 1998. In addition to chairman Simpson, the selection committee was composed of PDG Bob Lewis (Big Spring,) Mike Graves (Plainview,) Richard Griffith (Lubbock,) and Portuguese linguist Julia Trevino (Big Spring.) The Committee selected Richard Griffith (Lubbock) as the Rotarian Team Leader. Non-Rotarian team members included Michael Sawyer (Lubbock,) Toby McWilliams (Lubbock,) Cesar Caro (Sweetwater,) and Claudia Sorsby (Lubbock.) An alternate team member was Martha Loveless (Big Spring.)

Lynn also announced that the District 4750* Brazilian GSE team’s arrival date was May 7, 1998. Host clubs included those in Big Spring, Lubbock, Plainview, Pampa, Amarillo, and Midland. The team scheduled a visit to the 1998 District Conference in Ruidoso, NM. The GSE team leader was Rotarian Edson Peralva Barbirato, a cardiologist who was a member of the Rotary Club of Nova Friburgo, Brazil. The four other members of the team included Joseane Almeida Campos (professor,) Paulo Tannuri Costa (business administator,) Simone Fernandes de Andrade (computer systems analyst,) and Simone de Castro M. De Andrade (lawyer.)

My district in Brazil was the district 4750 and I was a member of the group in 1998; my name was changed by Paulo Tanuri (he was not a member of the GSE group and he has never traveled with the group). Rotarians in Snyder coordinated a project to feed approximately 300 of Scurry County’s less fortunate on Thanksgiving Day, 1997. Jim Boren, project chairman for the Snyder Rotary Club, reported that those helping with the dinner included the Snyder Ministerial Alliance, Lawrence IGA Grocery, The Shack, the Snyder High School Student Council, the Snyder ISD, and many Rotarian spouses.

Ted Holder (Levelland,) chair of the District International Service Committee described the group’s second trip that was made during Thanksgiving, 1997 to Arroyo Ancho, Mexico, a remote, mountainous area previously visited on many occasions by WCS teams from the district. The village of 107 people had acquired tubing and a tank for a water system but needed a pump to fill the tank. Ted paid for the pump with District matching grant funds, enjoyed Thanksgiving dinner with some of the villagers, and came home feeling very good about Rotary’s World Community Service opportunities.

PDG Doyle Moore reported that the Nominating Committee proposed Dudley Faver (Lubbock) as their recommendation for District Governor for the year 1999 – 2000. Dudley was an Assistant Governor during the current year.

By Christmas, 1997, Governor Roberts and Ramona had visited many clubs in the district on both official visits and special occasions. His official visits began in late August, 1997 and continued through early March, 1996. If anyone had concerns that the new district organization would deprive clubs of an association with the governor they learned otherwise during the year. At mid-year when asked for his reaction to the new District Leadership plan Governor Roberts responded:

“One of the most exciting things that has happened to me as District Governor of District 5730 has been the implementation of the NEW DISTRICT LEADERSHIP PLAN. I was fortunate enough to be the Governor when this plan was implemented by Rotary International.”

“The old plan, which served Rotary well, just could not keep pace with all the programs that Rotary International was promoting throughout the Rotary world. The district governor was unable, with just one visit per year to keep all the Rotary Clubs abreast of everything going on at Rotary International. With the advent of the Assistant District Governors, Rotary International, through the District Governor, is able to keep the clubs abreast of al phases of Rotary.”

 “The NEW DISTRICT LEADERSHIP PLAN enables every club to be visited by the Assistant District Governor in person every three months plus contact them by phone or letter monthly. Also, the District Governor will visit each club at least once in his term as District Governor. I feel this keeps our 53 clubs up to date on all phases of Rotary and Rotary International feels an informed club is a much better club. So far, in my year as District Governor I believe this is true. I also believe when this year is over every phase of activity within the district will show a healthy increase.”

Rotary International’s Council on Legislation was held in Delhi, India January 12 – 15, 1998. District 5730’s delegate to the council was PDG Doyle Moore (Amarillo.) His wife, Doris, accompanied him. During the four days members of the Council considered 196 proposed enactments, eleven amendments to those enactments, and 51 proposed resolutions, each designed to change some aspect of how Rotary operates. As in past Councils many items on the agenda were withdrawn, dropped, or voted down, but some passed making necessary a reprinting of a new Manual of Procedure for 1998 – 2001. A widespread PolioPlus immunization clinic was conducted in villages throughout India during the Council and many delegates participated in it one Sunday during their stay, including PDG Moore.

Governor Roberts reported in his Feb. newsletter that DGN Heetland (Amarillo West,) DGND Dudley Faver (Lubbock,) and he had held three meetings in January with area club presidents, president-elects, and Assistant Governors. These meetings were held in Lubbock, Amarillo, and Midland and allowed participants to become personally acquainted, set goals for coming years, and learn about the District Leadership Plan.

Doris Reding (Levelland) and Pat Davis (Childress,) Co-Chairs of the District Literacy Committee announced plans for a reading symposium on literacy in May, 1998 and called for Rotarians in the District to support their efforts to promote literacy projects and make known their interests in this area.

Stacy Ream (Plainview) announced that District 5730 was entering the ‘information age’ with a new District Web Page very soon. His goal was to increase communication access between Rotarians while providing Rotary information about all facets of the District. The Rotary Club of Amarillo was in the process of building a web page and Stacy urged all other clubs in the District to do so.

Edouard Beround, a French ambassadorial scholarship recipient who spent a year studying at Texas Tech during the 1995 - 1996 academic year, reported that he had been appointed by an American company that sells animal nutrition products throughout the world to be their representative in a territory that included France, Italy, and Spain. He attributed much of his career success to Rotary and his studies at Texas Tech.

Raymond Lusk, Lockney Rotary Club president, Governor J. B. Roberts, and members of the Lockney Rotary Club celebrated January 23, 1998 by proclaiming it “Owen and Kathleen Thornton” Day throughout the District. The occasion marked their tribute to the Thorntons for their 27 years of leadership and service to Rotary, its ideals, and its programs.

Rodney Hayes, president of the Kermit Rotary Club announced that their Tree Farm project got a substantial boost when a city block of land was donated to the club for use as a nursery. The club fenced the land, installed a drip irrigation system, planted 500 trees, added a large storage building, and laid plans to plant an additional 500 trees. With cooperation from the City of Kermit, a local garden club, and the school system, trees from the project will be transplanted throughout the city.


The Calendar of Events for the second half of Governor Roberts’ year contained the following items:


February SCRYE (Youth Ex.) 6-8, Tulsa, OK
March International Assembly & Institute,
6-13, Anaheim, CA
Lone Star PETS, 27-29, Dallas, TX
April District Assembly, 18th, Plainview, TX
May District Conference, 29-31, Ruidoso, NM
June R.I. Convention, 14-17, Indianapolis, IN

And so this recital arrived at it’s closing point, reminiscent of events of the past that shaped the world, filled with tales of deeds of Rotarians, some great, some minuscule, and leaving the author obstinately committed to the idea that Rotary helps us to be the best of who we are and accomplish with finesse those things that we do. Our obligation to those who preceded us remains unfulfilled, yet a stockastic mood prevails. The urge, not to simply recall the past but examine its applicability to the future, is strong. To be sure, the saga of mankind will continue, Rotary and Rotarians will pursue their objectives, and without doubt the illumination of the future will shine brightly on the hopes and dreams of those currently at work on the ideals of service.

APPENDIX I

REX WEBSTER
PAST DISTRICT GOVERNOR
PAST ROTARY INTERNATIONAL DIRECTOR AND VICE PRESIDENT
A PARTIAL LIST OF HIS WORK IN ROTARY

Madge Webster, wife of Rex Webster, was asked to provide a brief account of Rex’s involvement in Rotary. Upon reflection. the request was asking for a massive amount of searching through boxes of Rex’s records, for a biography of his activities in Rotary was not available. Her many house of combing the files plus her personal recollections produced the following account. Madge’s memory was superb but she cautioned that there were many omissions in her account. Rex’s association with Rotary began in January, 1941 and ended with his death on September 1, 1989. In this time span of forty-eight years, nine months of perfect attendance Rex, with Madge by his side, experienced Rotary from inductee to the highest echelons of the organization. For many years Rex refused to accept the nomination for President of Rotary International for reasons that were personal but frustrating to his multitude of friends in Rotary. He served as president of the Rotary Club of Lubbock 1947-48, District Governor 1956-57, and ten years later was on the Board of Directors of Rotary International. During his years in Rotary he spent countless hours on club, district, zone and Rotary International projects and activities. Following are some of Madge’s recollections.

The Rotary Club of Lubbock

Rex and Madge attended many other Conferences in addition to those listed above. He often functioned as Counselor, conference song leader, and spokesman for the Rotary Foundation. Rex was insistent that he not be scheduled as a Special Representative during our own Conference and he seldom missed one. Rex was District 573’s representative at several of R.I.’s Councils On Legislation.

Zone 1 and Zone 5 & 11

The first Zone Meeting ever held in Rotary was a small affair for PDG’s convened by Zone I R.I. Director Bill Walk in 1965 at an airport hotel at Los Angeles. Rex was there and he and Madge attended succeeding Zone 1 meetings. In 1967 and 1968 as R.I. Director Rex convened two consecutive Zone 1 meetings, both in Las Vegas, and added some training for incoming Governors and their spouses. Zone meetings became popular affairs and grew into substantial training sessions for incoming officers and PDG’s. When District 573 was reassigned to Zone 5, Rex and Madge attended those meetings and continued to attend the Zone 1 conferences because of old friendships. They attended other Zone meetings as well, often to represent the Foundation, a committee of R.I., or because a friend asked them to come.

Rex served on the Nominating Committee for President of R.I. on several occasions. He also was a member of the Nominating Committee for Director in both Zone I and Zone 5 a number of times.
